NONE
1.2 System Firmware
All products seeking OCP Accepted™ Product Recognition must complete the Open System Firmware (OSF) Tab in
the OCP Open Platform Firmware 2021 Supplier Requirements Checklist. The completed checklist shall be
uploaded and available
at: https://github.com/opencomputeproject/OpenSystemFirmware/[vendor_name]/[product_name]/.
Note to author: replace [vendor_name] and [product_name] with actual company name and product identifier.
2 Overview
This document is to define the requirements for a Datacenter NVMe SSD (DSSD) for use in datacenters. The
requirements in this document are in addition to the requirements in the underlying standards and may override
some requirements in the underlying standards. The authors have attempted to note where requirements may
be incompatible with the underlying standards.
If functionality in an underlying standard (e.g., a command) is not covered in this document, then the
requirements in the underlying standard apply. For example, if an optional command in an underlying standard
is not covered in this document, then that command remains optional.
Customers may impose additional requirements beyond those specified in this document.
3 Scope
This document covers PCIe-attached SSDs using NVM Express.
6

4 NVM Express Requirements
4.1 Overview
Requirement ID Description
The device shall comply with all required features of the NVM Express Base Specification
Revision 2.2, the NVM Express NVM Command Set Specification Revision 1.1, and the NVM
Express NVMe over PCIe Transport Specification Revision 1.2, or later except as overridden
NVMe-1
by this specification. Optional features in those three specifications shall be implemented
per the requirements of this specification based on the three specifications above. The
vendor shall provide an NVMe compliance report that demonstrates compliance.
Any optional NVMe features supported by the device not described in this document shall
NVMe-2
be clearly documented and disclosed to the customer.
Any vendor unique features supported by the device not described in this document shall
NVMe-3
be clearly documented and disclosed to the customer.
4.2 NVMe Reset Supported
Requirement ID Description
NVMeR-1 NVM Subsystem Reset (NSSR) shall be supported via the NSSRC register.
NVMeR-2 NVMe Controller Reset (CC.EN cleared from 1b to 0b) shall be supported.
4.3 NVMe Controller Configuration and Behavior
Requirement ID Description
The default arbitration shall be Round-Robin. Weighted Round Robin with Urgent Class
NVMe-CFG-1
Priority shall be supported.
NVMe-CFG-2 The device shall support a Maximum Data Transfer Size (MDTS) value of at least 256 KiB.
NVMe-CFG-3 The device firmware shall support the use of CSTS.CFS.
NVMe-CFG-4 Obsolete. Replaced by LABL-11.
NVMe-CFG-5 The minimum supported queue depth shall be 1,024 per submission queue.
NVMe-CFG-6 The minimum number of I/O Queue Pairs shall be 1,023.
The single default namespace (see SECTOR-3) shall have a unique non-zero value in the
EUI64 (Extended Unique Identifier) field in the Identify Namespace data structure.
For each namespace that is created other than the initial namespace configured in the
NVMe-CFG-7
factory, the device shall clear the EUI64 field to 0h in the Identify Namespace data structure.
This requirement is specific to the value of the EUI64 field in the Identify Namespace data
structure and has no effect on the value of the NGUID field in that data structure.
7

Requirement ID Description
The device shall support a non-zero NGUID per Namespace and shall never reuse any
NVMe-CFG-8 NGUID value (i.e., the UIDREUSE bit in the Common Namespace Features field of the
Identify Namespace data structure shall be set to 1b).
The Doorbell Stride field in the Controller Capabilities data structure (CAP.DSTRD) shall be
NVMe-CFG-9
cleared to 0h.
The device shall align the start of the Doorbells to a 4096-byte boundary as per the PCI
NVMe-CFG-10
Express Base Specification and the NVM Express Base Specification.
If the Controller Memory Buffer (CMB) is supported, then the implementation shall comply
with TP4054, which is included in the NVMe Express Base Specification 1.4 and subsequent
NVMe-CFG-11
versions (see NVMe-1). This includes the requirement that the CMB shall be disabled by
default.
The Controller Power Scope field in the Controller Capabilities property shall be set to a
NVMe-CFG-12 value of 11b to indicate it is NVM subsystem scope (i.e., the NVM subsystem does not
support multiple power domains).
The device shall support the NVM Command Set (i.e., in the Command Sets Supported field
in the Controller Capabilities (CAP) property bit 0 shall be set to 1b, bit 6 shall be cleared to
NVMe-CFG-13
0b, and bit 7 shall be cleared to 0b, and the Controller Type field in the Identify Controller
data structure shall be set to 01h).
The device shall support a maximum Submission Queue Entry Size of 64 bytes (i.e., bits 7:4
NVMe-CFG-14
of the SQES field in the Identify Controller data structure shall be set to 6).
The device shall support a maximum Completion Queue Entry Size of 16 bytes (i.e., bits 7:4
NVMe-CFG-15
of the CQES field in the Identify Controller data structure shall be set to 4).
The device shall clear the Memory Page Size Minimum (MPSMIN) field to 0h (4 KiB
NVMe-CFG-16
minimum page size).
The device shall set the Memory Page Size Maximum (MPSMAX) field to a value of 1h or
NVMe-CFG-17
greater (8 KiB or greater maximum page size).
NVMe-CFG-18 The device shall support 256 Error Log Page Entries.
The device shall clear the Host Memory Buffer Minimum Size field and the Host Memory
NVMe-CFG-19 Buffer Preferred Size field in the Identify Controller data structure to 0h (i.e., the Host
Memory Buffer feature shall not be supported).
NVMe-CFG-20 The device shall clear the CAP.CRMS.CRIMS bit to 0b.
NVMe-CFG-21 The device shall support Power Measurement (See TP4199).
NVMe-CFG-22 The device shall not write to any memory in any Submission Queue (SQ).
NVMe-CFG-23 The device shall not read from any memory in any Completion Queue (CQ).
The device shall meet full performance under the following conditions when not limited by
host performance:
NVMe-CFG-24
• a single SQ/CQ pair with a max queue depth of 1024;
• an Arbitration burst of at most 8 commands (RAB = 3);
8

Requirement ID Description
• a PCIe Payload Size of 512 bytes or less; and
• device formatted to 4KiB LBAs.
4.4 NVMe Admin Command Set
The device shall support the following mandatory and optional NVMe Admin commands:
Requirement ID Description
NVMe-AD-1 The device shall support all mandatory NVMe Admin commands.
Identify – In addition to supporting all the mandatory CNS values and the associated
mandatory fields within the data returned for each mandatory CNS value, the following
optional fields shall be supported:
• Format progress indicator (FPI) with an update granularity of 1% in the Identify
NVMe-AD-2 Namespace data structure in the NVM Command Set and in the I/O Command Set
Independent Identify Namespace data structure.
• I/O Performance and Endurance Hints:
o bit 4 (OPTPERF) shall be set to 1b in the Namespace Features (NSFEAT) field
in the Identify Namespace data structure for the NVM Command Set.
NVMe-AD-3 The Namespace Management command shall be supported.
NVMe-AD-4 The Namespace Attachment command shall be supported.
The Format NVM command shall be supported. Secure Erase Settings (SES) values 000b,
NVMe-AD-5
001b and 010b shall be supported.
The device shall support the NVMe-MI Receive and NVMe-MI Send commands (i.e., bit 6 in
the Optional Admin Command Support field in the Identify Controller data structure shall be
NVMe-AD-6
set to 1b). The device shall support all NVMe-MI commands that map to the NVMe-MI
Receive command and that are mandatory using the in-band tunneling mechanism.
The device shall support the Sanitize command and the Sanitize Status Log Page (81h). The
device shall support Block Erase (010b), Overwrite (011b), and Crypto Erase (100b) sanitize
NVMe-AD-7
operations. The Sanitize Namespace command defined in TP4153 is optional for the device
to support.
Once data is purged (see SEC-43) due to:
• a Sanitize command that requests a sanitize operation and has the No-Deallocate
After Sanitize bit cleared to 0b;
• a Sanitize command that requests a Block Erase (SANACT=001b) or Crypto Erase
(SANACT=100b) sanitize operation and has the No-Deallocate After Sanitize bit set
NVMe-AD-8 to 1b but resulted in a deallocate for the reason specified in NVMe-AD-19;
• a Format NVM command that specifies User Data Erase or Cryptographic Erase; or
• a TCG Revert method, RevertSP method or GenKey method,
the device shall deallocate all user data, enable reads to the purged/deallocated LBAs
without generating errors, and return all zeroes for host reads to LBAs that have not been
written since the last such purge completed.
9

Requirement ID Description
Once data is purged (see SEC-43) due to a Sanitize command that requests an Overwrite
(SANACT=011b) sanitize operation, and has the No-Deallocate After Sanitize bit set to 1b,
the device shall not deallocate any user data, shall enable reads to the overwritten LBAs
without generating errors, and shall return the bytes written by the last overwrite pass for
host reads to LBAs that have not been written since the last such purge completed.
NVMe-AD-9 Obsolete. Incorporated into NVMe-AD-8.
NVMe-AD-10 The device shall support Identify command UUID List functionality (CNS value 17h).
If the Namespace Identifier (NSID) is not used for a specific NVMe Admin command, and the
NVMe-AD-11 host specifies a non-zero NSID, then the controller shall abort the command with status
Invalid Field in Command.
NVMe-AD-12 The Device Self-test command shall be supported.
NVMe-AD-13 Obsolete. See SELFTST-8.
The device shall support the Lockdown command. For device profile specific requirements
NVMe-AD-14
see DP-CFG-11.
The Lockdown command shall support locking down all supported Admin commands on the
NVMe-AD-15 in-band interface including the Lockdown command itself and all Admin commands not
referenced in this specification.
The Lockdown command shall support locking down all supported Features on the in-band
NVMe-AD-16
interface, including those not referenced in this specification.
The device shall set the No-Deallocate Modifies Media After Sanitize field to 01b in the
NVMe-AD-17 Sanitize Capabilities in the Identify Controller data structure. Additional media modification
after Sanitize is prohibited.
The device shall clear the No-Deallocate Inhibited bit to 0b in the Sanitize Capabilities in the
NVMe-AD-18
Identify Controller data structure.
If the device cannot return logical block data due to checksum errors after a sanitize
operation successfully completes that had been started by a Sanitize command with the No-
Deallocate After Sanitize bit set to 1b, then the device shall instead perform a deallocation
NVMe-AD-19 even though it was requested not to deallocate and shall set the Sanitize Status field to 100b
in the Sanitize Status log page upon successful completion of the sanitize operation and
deallocation. This behavior overrides the requirements in the NVM Express Base
Specification.
NVMe-AD-20 Obsolete. Incorporated into NVMe-AD-8.
The device shall not write data to any namespace user data in the NVM subsystem as part of
NVMe-AD-21 a Crypto Erase sanitize operation, Block Erase sanitize operation, Format NVM Cryptographic
Erase, Format NVM User Data Erase, or TCG Opal Revert/RevertSP/GenKey method.
The device shall be shipped from the factory with the Sanitize Status field in the Sanitize
NVMe-AD-22 Status log page cleared to 000b indicating the NVM subsystem has never been sanitized and
the Global Data Erased bit in the Sanitize Status field set to 1b.
10

Requirement ID Description
The device shall support the Format NVM command on a per namespace basis (i.e., bit 0
NVMe-AD-23
and bit 1 shall be cleared to 00b in the Format NVM Attributes field in Identify Controller).
The device shall report a minimum value of 3 in the Asynchronous Event Request Limit field
NVMe-AD-24 in the Identify Controller data structure to indicate support for at least 4 outstanding
Asynchronous Event Request commands.
If asynchronous events occur for which reporting is enabled and there are no Asynchronous
Event Request commands outstanding, then the controller shall retain the event
information for those Asynchronous Event Types and use that information for responses to
NVMe-AD-25 future Asynchronous Event Request commands. Queued duplicate Asynchronous events
shall be reported once.
This requirement does not apply to Immediate (asynchronous) events, as Immediate events
are never queued.
The device shall support Media Verification for entire device sanitize operations initiated by
NVMe-AD-26
the Sanitize command.
The device is not required to support the Get LBA Status command. The device shall
NVMe-AD-27
support the related LBA Status Information log page, see STD-LOG-11.
The device shall clear the DAE bit to 0b in the NSFEAT field in Identify Namespace to indicate
NVMe-AD-28 that the device does not support the Deallocated or Unwritten Logical Block error for any
namespace.
The device shall support both the 0b and 1b values of the No-Deallocate After Sanitize bit in
the Sanitize command. If the No-Deallocate After Sanitize bit is cleared to 0b in a Sanitize
NVMe-AD-29 command, then the device shall deallocate all LBAs upon completion of the sanitize
operation, including media verification (see NVMe-AD-26), if performed as part of the
sanitize operation.
The controller shall delete all queued Asynchronous Event Notifications upon Power Cycle or
NVMe-AD-30
Controller Level Reset events.
For the DSSD Error Reporting asynchronous event, the default value for the DSSD
NVMe-AD-31 Asynchronous Event Configuration feature (Feature Identifier C9h) shall be set to 1 (i.e.,
enabled). See GDAEC-2.
For the DSSD Media Ready asynchronous event, the default value for the DSSD
NVMe-AD-32 Asynchronous Event Configuration feature (Feature Identifier C9h) shall be cleared to 0 (i.e.,
disabled). See GDAEC-3.
If the device is able to perform a Cryptographic Erase for a Format NVM command that
requests User Data Erase (SES=001b), then the device shall:
• support Cryptographic Erase functionality (SES=010b) for Format NVM commands;
NVMe-AD-33
and
• perform a cryptographic erase for any Format NVM command that requests User
Data Erase.
11

4.4.1 Namespace Management/Attachment Commands
The namespace management command along with the attach/detach commands is used to increase device over-
provisioning beyond the default minimum over-provisioning.
Requirement ID Description
NSM-1 The namespace management commands shall be supported on all namespaces.
When creating a namespace, the default “Formatted LBA Size” parameter (FLBAS = 0) in the
NSM-2 Identify Namespace Data Structure (byte 26) shall correspond to the default sector size set
at the factory.
The LBA Format 0 Support field shall correspond to the default sector size set at the factory
NSM-3
(see DP-CFG-1).
NSM-4 The device shall support a minimum of 16 Namespaces (see Section 13 Device Profiles).
For some models (see Section 13 Device Profiles), the minimum number of namespaces
shall be at least 128 Namespaces at 7 TiB based on 16 Namespaces per TB of usable
capacity. The number of Namespaces shall be based on the device usable capacity as
follows:
Device Usable Capacity Minimum Number of Namespaces
<= 1 TiB 16
NSM-5
> 1 TiB but <= 2 TiB 32
> 2 TiB but <= 3 TiB 48
> 3 TiB but <= 4 TiB 64
… …
> 7 TiB 128
The device shall report at least one Namespace Granularity Descriptor in the Namespace
NSM-6
Granularity List.
The device shall support the TNVMCAP and UNVMCAP fields in the Identify Controller Data
NSM-7
Structure.
The device shall not support extended LBA formats (i.e., the Extended LBA Formats
NSM-8 Supported bit in the Controller Attributes register in the Identify Controller data structure
shall be cleared to ‘0’).
4.4.2 Namespace Utilization (NUSE)
Requirement ID Description
The NUSE shall be equal to the number of logical blocks currently allocated in the
namespace. NUSE cannot be hardcoded to be equal to NCAP. Here is an example for a
NUSE-1 200 GB device:
1. After a Format NVM command User Data Erase (SES = 001b), NUSE would be zero.
And the usage data would reflect that: 0.00 GB.
12

Requirement ID Description
2. After writing 1 GB worth of data, the usage data is expected to show the following:
1.00 GB.
3. After filling the device, the usage data is expected to show the following: 200.00 GB.
4. If the host issues a 10 GB deallocate command and the device completes
deallocation of the data, the usage data would show the following: 190.00 GB.
Deallocation may occur in the background after completion of the deallocate command with
NUSE updated accordingly as deallocation occurs.

Identifiers used in this specification access the functionality defined in this specification (i.e., do not access other
vendor specific functionality that may use the same vendor specific identifiers).

The UUID List (NVMe-AD-10) shall contain a UUID List Entry that contains the UUID value
C194D55BE0944794A21D29998F56BE6Fh in big endian format. The Identifier Association
field in that UUID List Entry shall be cleared to 00b.

4.4.4 DSSD Asynchronous Events
This section describes the Asynchronous Event Notifications defined by this specification.
Requirement ID Description
If the device uses the Error Reporting AEN to report an error condition and the device
encounters an error condition, then the device shall complete an Asynchronous Event
Request (AER) command with an Asynchronous Event Notification (AEN) with Completion
Queue Entry Dword 0 set as follows:
DSSD-AEN-1 • The Log Page Identifier field shall be set to C1h.
• The Asynchronous Event Information field shall be set to 01h.
• The Asynchronous Event Type field shall be set to 111b (Vendor Specific).
• The device shall process an Error Reporting AEN as a Notice event (e.g., queued if
there is not an outstanding AER command).
If the device uses the Media Ready AEN to report that the media is ready to process
commands and the Media Ready Event occurs, the device shall complete an Asynchronous
Event Request (AER) command with an Asynchronous Event Notification (AEN) with
Completion Queue Entry Dword 0 set as follows:
DSSD-AEN-2 • The Log Page Identifier field shall be cleared to 00h.
• The Asynchronous Event Information field shall be set to 01h.
• The Asynchronous Event Type field shall be set to 111b (Vendor Specific).
The device shall process a Media Ready AEN as a One-Shot event (e.g., queued if there is no
outstanding AER command).
14

4.5 NVMe I/O Command Set
Requirement ID Description
NVMe-IO-1 The device shall support all mandatory NVMe I/O commands.
The device shall support the Dataset Management command. For additional information
NVMe-IO-2
see TRIM-1.
Since the device is power fail safe (e.g., has Power Loss Protection (PLP)) the performance
shall not be degraded by any of the following:
• FUA – i.e., forced unit access shall not incur a performance penalty.
• Flush Cache – i.e., flush cache shall have no effect as the PLP makes any cache non-
NVMe-IO-3
volatile.
• Volatile Write Cache (Feature Identifier 06h) Set Features to disable write-cache.
This command shall fail as described in the NVM Express Base Specification as there
is no volatile write cache.
The device shall support the Write Zeroes command and shall set bit 3 of the ONCS field to
1b. The following bits of the Write Zeroes command shall be supported:
NVMe-IO-4
• Deallocate (DEAC) bit.
• Force Unit Access (FUA) bit.
The Write Zeroes command shall have the following behavior:
DEAC FUA Behavior
The device shall follow the NVM Express NVM Command Set
0b 0b
Specification, see NVMe-1.
NVMe-IO-5 The device shall follow the NVM Express NVM Command Set
0b 1b
Specification, see NVMe-1.
The device shall follow the NVM Express NVM Command Set
1b 1b
Specification, see NVMe-1.
1b 0b See NVMe-IO-6.
If the Write Zeroes DEAC bit is set to 1b and the FUA bit is cleared to 0b, the device shall
deallocate the specified LBAs and shall return all zeros for any subsequent read to the
NVMe-IO-6
specified LBAs until modified by a command (e.g., Write, Copy, etc.), regardless of the
behavior of the Dataset Management command.
With the DEAC bit set to 1b and the FUA bit cleared to 0b one or more Write Zeroes
command(s) whose data size is the maximum value that is less than or equal to the data
size:
• indicated by the value of the Write Zeroes Size Limit (WZSL) field in the Identify
NVMe-IO-7 Controller Data Structure for the NVM command set if that WZSL field is set to a
non-zero value; or
• that results from the maximum value of the NLB field in the Write Zeroes command
for a namespace that uses the factory default sector size (see DP-CFG-1) if that
WZSL field is cleared to zero,
15

Requirement ID Description
shall be able to completely deallocate the entire device including updating the FTL map
(e.g., in memory) so that subsequent reads return all zeroes as required by NVMe-IO-6 in
less than one minute.
NVMe-IO-8 The device shall support the Compare command.
NVMe-IO-9 The device shall support the Compare and Write fused command pair.
For some models (see Section 13 Device Profiles), the device shall support the Write
NVMe-IO-10
Uncorrectable command.
The Write Uncorrectable command shall support marking LBAs uncorrectable at a single LBA
NVMe-IO-11
granularity regardless of the number of LBAs in the FTL indirection granularity.
The device shall not limit the number of LBAs that the host is able to specify in a Write
Uncorrectable command beyond the minimum and maximum allowed by the NVM Express
NVMe-IO-12
NVM Command Set Specification. The device shall support Write Uncorrectable commands
that specify a single LBA.
There shall be no limit on the total media capacity that can be marked uncorrectable by
NVMe-IO-13
Write Uncorrectable commands.
Uncorrectable errors (e.g., read errors) that are a consequence of a prior Write
NVMe-IO-14 Uncorrectable command shall not be counted in the SMART / Health Information log page
(Log Identifier 02h) Media and Data Integrity Errors field.
NVMe-IO-15 The device shall support SGLs for all I/O commands.
NVMe-IO-16 The device shall support SGL Descriptor Type 0, 1, 2 and 3.
The device shall configure SGLS (SGL Support) 2-bit field in the SGLS Dword field in the
NVMe-IO-17 Identify Controller Data Structure to a value of 01b (byte alignment) or 10b (Dword
alignment). Host code should use Dword alignment regardless of this field value.
The device shall set the MPTR SGL Descriptor Support (MSDS) bit to 1b in the Identify
NVMe-IO-18
Controller Data Structure.
4.6 Optional NVMe Feature Support
The device shall also support the following NVMe features:
Requirement ID Description
NVMe-OPT-1 Obsolete. Duplicate of STD-LOG-7 and STD-LOG-8.
The device shall support the Timestamp feature (Feature Identifier 0Eh). Timestamps are
NVMe-OPT-2
used to align the devices internal logs.
NVMe-OPT-3 Obsolete. See TEL-5.
If a timestamp has been set via Set Features for the Timestamp feature (Feature Identifier
0Eh), then:
NVMe-OPT-4
a) the device shall maintain the timestamp across all Controller Level Resets other
than a Controller Level Reset caused by an NVM Subsystem Reset (i.e., if a
16

Requirement ID Description
timestamp has been set, then it is only permissible to clear the Timestamp Origin

b) saving the timestamp across an NVM Subsystem Reset is optional.
The device shall never set the Synch field bit to 1b in the Timestamp feature (Feature
NVMe-OPT-5
Identifier 0Eh).
The device shall only generate a Telemetry Log Changed event on an error condition and
NVMe-OPT-6

Attributes field in the Identify Controller data structure).
NVMe-OPT-13 The Timestamp feature (Feature Identifier 0Eh) shall not be saveable.
The device shall ignore the values in reserved bits and fields received in commands or
NVMe-OPT-14 register writes (i.e., the device shall not generate an error because a reserved bit or field is
not cleared to zero).

NVMe-OPT-18
TP4199.

TP4199.

Requirement ID Description

or smaller.

TP4190.

NVMe-OPT-22
(NPWG) to enable writing of NPWG sized chunks of data without read/modify/write.
4.7 Command Timeout
Requirement ID Description
NVMe Admin commands and TCG commands shall take no more than 10 seconds from
submission to completion. This CTO-1 requirement does not apply to the time taken by
CTO-1
background operations (e.g., Device Self-test and Sanitize commands). This CTO-1
requirement does not apply to Asynchronous Event Request commands.
In addition to the Asynchronous Event Request command, the only other exception to the
CTO-1 requirement shall be the Format NVM Command for non-Cryptographic Erase
CTO-2
operations. Format NVM Cryptographic Erase and the TCG methods Revert, RevertSP and
GenKey shall comply with the CTO-1 requirement.
Once the TTR-2 requirement is satisfied, an individual I/O command (submitted under
CTO-3 Queue Depth 1) shall take no more than 8 seconds from submission to completion. Under
full load the device shall not have more than 7 I/Os take more than 2 seconds in one hour.
CTO-4 I/O command processing time shall not be a function of device capacity.
The vendor shall disclose any I/O scenario that could violate the timeout requirements in
CTO-5
CTO-1 through CTO-4.
The device shall set MDTS, the attributes of the Number of Queues feature (Feature
CTO-6 Identifier 07h) and Maximum Queue Entries Supported such that the CTO-3 requirement
cannot be violated.
A Crypto Erase sanitize operation, and any background activity initiated by a TCG command
CTO-7
(e.g., as indicated by OutstandingData) shall complete within 10 seconds.
A Block Erase sanitize operation and a Format NVM command performing a User Data Erase
CTO-8 shall each complete within 10 seconds per TB of device capacity (e.g., a Block Erase sanitize
operation on a 4TB device shall complete within 40 seconds).
The device shall report the greater of the Sanitize Crypto Erase, Format NVM Cryptographic
CTO-9 Erase, TCG Opal Revert, TCG Opal RevertSP, or TCG Opal GenKey time in the Estimated Time
for Crypto Erase field in the Sanitize Status log page.
The device shall not set the Estimated Time fields in the Sanitize Status log page to a value
CTO-10
of FFFFFFFFh for supported sanitize operations.
18

Requirement ID Description
Formats between LBAF values with the Secure Erase Settings field cleared to 000b (No
CTO-11 secure erase operation requested) or 2h (Cryptographic Erase) shall complete within 10
seconds.
4.8 Log Page Requirements
4.8.1 Standard Log Page Requirements
Requirement ID Description
STD-LOG-1 The device shall support the Error Information log page (Log Identifier 01h).
STD-LOG-2 The device shall support the SMART / Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h).
Under no conditions shall the Percentage Used field in the SMART / Health Information log
STD-LOG-3
page (Log Identifier 02h) decrease to a lower value than previously reported.
The Percentage Used field in the SMART / Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h)
shall be based on the average P/E cycle of the device. In addition, this field shall be based
STD-LOG-4
on the actual P/E cycle count of the media and not on the Power on Hours (POH) of the
device.
STD-LOG-5 The device shall support the Firmware Slot Information log page (Log Identifier 03h).
STD-LOG-6 The device shall support the Commands Supported and Effects log page (Log Identifier 05h).
STD-LOG-7 The device shall support the Telemetry Host-Initiated log page (Log Identifier 07h).
STD-LOG-8 The device shall support the Telemetry Controller-Initiated log page (Log Identifier 08h).
STD-LOG-9 The device shall support the Persistent Event log page (Log Identifier 0Dh).
The device shall support the following Persistent Event Log types:
Type Event
01h SMART / Health Log Snapshot

execution (see Section 4.8.2 TCG Events for Persistent Event Log and Section

Fatal.

STD-LOG-11
device is not required to support the related Get LBA Status command (see NVMe-AD-27).
The following behavior types are used to define the functional boundary condition
behaviors for saturating or wrapping, under reset conditions and power cycles:

counter, “Yes” indicates saturating behavior (i.e., report all F’s if the value exceeds
the maximum possible value of the field or statistic).
2.  All Controller Level Resets (e.g., Controller Reset, NVM Subsystem Reset, PCIe
Function Level Reset, PCIe Conventional Reset, etc.).
For Behavior Types 1 the counter shall reset to zero only on a Controller Level Reset,
including any CLR caused by a Power Cycle or PERST#.  For Behavior Type 6 the counter shall
reset to zero only on a Power Cycle or PERST#.
STD-LOG-13  The device shall support the Device Self-test log page (Log Identifier 06h).
STD-LOG-14  The device shall support the Command and Feature Lockdown log page (Log Identifier 14h).
The device shall support the Physical Interface Receiver Eye Opening Measurement log page
STD-LOG-15
(Log Identifier 19h).
20

Requirement ID Description
In addition to any receiver margining data and image plots, the device shall store
information required to evaluate the signal integrity of the receiver such as equalization
STD-LOG-16 values like continuous time linear equalization (CTLE), variable gain amplifier (VGA), boost,
and decision feedback equalization (DFE) settings in the Eye Data field of the Physical
Interface Receiver Eye Opening Measurement log page.
The device shall support the Endurance Group Information log page (Log Identifier 09h).
STD-LOG-17 The device shall use a single Endurance Group for the entire device. The device is not
required to support the Endurance Group Event Aggregate log page (Log Identifier 0Fh).
The device shall not support the SMART / Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h)
STD-LOG-18 on a per namespace basis (i.e., bit 0 of the Log Page Attributes field in the Identify Controller
data structure shall be cleared to 0b).
The Persistent Event log page (Log Identifier 0Dh), Telemetry Host-Initiated log page (Log
Identifier 07h), Telemetry Controller-Initiated log page (Log Identifier 08h), and Error
STD-LOG-19
Information log page (Log Identifier 01h) shall not contain user data, or the result of any
computation performed on user data.
The Persistent Event log page (Log Identifier 0Dh) events shall be ordered so that the more
recent events are reported earlier in the log than older events (i.e., the most recent event is
STD-LOG-20 Persistent Event 0), and the events deemed less important by the vendor (e.g., old events,
informational events, etc.) are removed first when the log is trimmed due to lack of space to
store all events).
The Persistent Event log page (Log Identifier 0Dh) reporting context shall be held until
released by the host or until at least 5 minutes has elapsed since the last host access of the
STD-LOG-21 log unless the log fills and reporting context has to be released in order to remove events
(see STD-LOG-20). New events that occur while the context is established shall not be
dropped.
The maximum size of the Persistent Event log page (Log Identifier 0Dh) reported in the
STD-LOG-22 Persistent Event Log Size (PELS) field in the Identify Controller data structure shall be 5 MiB
or greater.
The device shall not lose log page data for any reason, unless otherwise specified (e.g., see
STD-LOG-20 and the purge exception in this requirement).
Data that does not contain user data or data that could be used to derive user data
including the Telemetry Host-Initiated log page (Log Identifier 07h), Telemetry Controller-
Initiated log page (Log Identifier 08h), Persistent Event log page (Log Identifier 0Dh), Error
Information log page (Log Identifier 01h), vendor-specific log pages, SMART / Health
Information log page (Log Identifier 02h) including the Critical Warnings field, SMART /
STD-LOG-23
Health Information Extended log page (Log Identifier C0h), and backup energy source failure
information shall be persisted across purge operations (see SEC-43).
All log page data including the Telemetry Host-Initiated log page (Log Identifier 07h),
Telemetry Controller-Initiated log page (Log Identifier 08h), Persistent Event log page (Log
Identifier 0Dh), Error Information log page (Log Identifier 01h), vendor-specific log pages,
SMART / Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h) including the Critical Warnings
field, SMART / Health Information Extended log page (Log Identifier C0h), and backup
21

Requirement ID Description
energy source failure information shall be persisted across power loss, all resets, the Format
NVM command, and the device entering any protected mode (e.g., read only or error
mode).
Issues with the device’s encryption engine shall not prevent access to the data specified by
this requirement.
STD-LOG-24 The device shall support the Power Measurement log page (Log Identifier 25h).
The device shall configure the Power Management Attributes (PMA) field in the Power
Management Log as follows:

• Clear the Estimated Power Flag (EPF) to 0b
• Set the Maximum Interval Power Timestamp Support (MIPWRTS) to 1b

4.8.2 TCG Activity Events for Persistent Event Log
This defines the requirements for recording TCG Activity Events in the Persistent Event Log as Event Type DEh
(see STD-LOG-10).
Requirement ID Description
The device shall support recording at least 100 TCG Activity Events in the Persistent Event
TCGHST-PE-1
Log without deleting any TCG Activity Events to make room for new events.
A TCG Activity Event entry shall be recorded in the Persistent Event Log whenever any of the
following TCG activities occurs (the event is recorded upon completion of the activity):
• Level 0 Discovery
• Start Session
• Authenticate method (entries only recorded when the authority specified is not
locked out)
TCGHST-PE-2 • Close Session by the host when it sends an End-Of-Session token
• Close Session due to timeout
• Properties method
• Stack Reset
• TPer Reset
• Hardware Reset
• Get method
22

Requirement ID Description
• Set method
• GenKey method
• Random method
• Activate method
• Revert method
• RevertSP method
• Reactivate method
• Erase method
• Block SID Authentication
• Assign method
• Deassign method
Redundant TCG activities shall not generate new TCG Command Event entries in the
Persistent Event Log. A TCG activity shall be considered redundant if it meets ALL the
following criteria with respect to a TCG Activity Event that is already recorded in the
Persistent Event Log:
• Power cycle count is the same; and
• Active firmware revision is the same; and
• TCG activity is the same as the most recent TCG Activity Event entry; and
• Tper state remains the same (i.e., there has been no change either in the device
behavior or host visible state); and
TCGHST-PE-3
• The Result field is the same.
• The following are examples of TCG activities that do not generate a new TCG Activity
Event entry:
• Setting an attribute of a TCG Object to a value that is the same as the current value.
• Getting or setting the value of an informative attribute of a TCG object (e.g., the
CommonName of a Locking Object).
• Getting data from or setting data to byte tables.
• An unsuccessful authentication attempt that returns AUTHORITY_LOCKED_OUT
status.
TCG Activity Event entries shall not be removed for any TCG-specific reason (e.g., TCG
TCGHST-PE-4 Revert/RevertSP or TCG Manufactured-Inactive), except as required to make room in the
Persistent Event Log for additional TCG Activity Event entries (see TCGHST-PE-1).
TCG Activity Event format shall follow the requirements in the TCG Activity Event Format
TCGHST-PE-5
section.

Log Identifier Scope Log Page Name Reference Section
C4h NVM subsystem Device Capabilities 4.8.10
C5h NVM subsystem Unsupported Requirements 4.8.12
C6h NVM subsystem Hardware Component 4.8.13
C7h NVM subsystem TCG Configuration 4.8.14

KEY:
• Namespace = The log page contains information about a specific namespace.
• Controller = The log page contains information about the controller that is processing the
command.
• NVM subsystem = The log page contains information about the NVM subsystem.
The following table defines the interactions for all DSSD specific log pages with the Format NVM command and
sanitize operations:
Requirement ID Description
The DSSD log pages to which access is allowed during a Format NVM command or sanitize
operations are listed below. Note that this requirement requires vendor-specific log pages
to be accessible during a sanitize operation which overrides the requirement in the NVM
Express Base Specification to prohibit access to vendor-specific log pages during a sanitize
operation:

4.8.5 SMART / Health Information Requirements
The requirements for the SMART / Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h) and SMART / Health
Information Extended log page (Log Identifier C0h) are in Section 4.8.1 Standard Log Page Requirements and the
following table:
Requirement ID Description
All values in the DSSD log pages defined by this specification shall be persistent across
SLOG-1
power cycles unless otherwise specified.
27

Requirement ID Description
All counters defined by this specification shall be saturating counters (i.e., if the counter
SLOG-2 reaches the maximum allowable size, it stops incrementing and does NOT roll back to 0)
unless otherwise specified.
SLOG-3 All fields in DSSD log pages shall be little endian format.
A normalized counter defined by this specification, unless otherwise specified, shall be
reported as the following: 100% shall represent the number at factory exit. 1% shall
SLOG-4
represent the minimum amount for the device to be reliable. A value of 0% means the
device shall no longer be considered reliable. 100% shall be represented as 64h.
SLOG-5 The device shall support all fields in the SMART / Health Information log page.
A Get Log Page command for either the SMART /Health Information log page (Log Identifier
02h) or SMART / Health Information Extended log page (Log Identifier C0h) shall not require
SLOG-6
an update of the SMART values other than the temperature values in SLOG-8. It shall be a
simple read of the current data and shall not block I/O.
Unless otherwise specified, the device shall update the values of the SMART /Health
SLOG-7 Information log page (Log Identifier 02h) and SMART / Health Information Extended log
page (Log Identifier C0h) in the background at least once every ten minutes.
The composite and raw temperature sensor values shall be updated when the SMART /
SLOG-8
Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h) is accessed.
All assert events and controller-initiated log captures shall have an associated vendor-
SLOG-9
specific “Reason Identifier” that uniquely identifies the assert /controller condition.
SLOG-10 Obsolete (see STD-LOG-23).
SLOG-11 Obsolete (see STD-LOG-23).
The device shall not set any bits in the Critical Warning field in the SMART / Health
SLOG-12 Information log page (Log Identifier 02h) solely due to the value in the Percentage Used field
in the SMART/ Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h).
The device shall report lifetime energy in the Operational Lifetime Energy Consumed (OLEC)
SLOG-13
field in the SMART/ Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h).
The device shall configure the Interval Power Measurement (IPM) field in the SMART/
Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h) as follows:
• Clear the Power Measurement Type (PMT) to NVM Subsystem (0h).
SLOG-14
• Configure the Interval Power Measurement Scale (IPMS) field to 10b or 01b to
report a scale value.
• Report the Interval Power Measurement Value (IPMV) as a non-zero value.

This field is the normalized counter of the number of
NAND blocks which are currently erased and ready to be
written with user data, out of the total number of NAND
blocks in the spare area.  i.e., this is the percentage of
erased NAND blocks in spare area, where the spare area
is defined as the NAND blocks that contain no valid user
data, no valid system data, and are:
| SMART-17  | 120  | % Free Blocks  | 1   |     |
| --------- | ---- | -------------- | --- | --- |
•  waiting to be erased for use to write user data;
or
•  already erased and ready to be used to write
user data.
i.e., % Free Blocks = A / (A + B) where A is the number of
currently erased NAND blocks and B is the number of
NAND blocks waiting to be erased.
| SMART-18  | 127:121  | Reserved  | 7  Shall be cleared to zero.  |     |

This field is an indicator of the capacitor health and
represents the capacitor holdup energy margin during
operation.  If no PLP protection is present a value of
FFFFh shall be reported.  100% represents the passing
hold up energy threshold when a device leaves
|           |          | Capacitor  | manufacturing.  Thus, a device will typically report  |     |
| --------- | -------- | ---------- | ----------------------------------------------------- | --- |
| SMART-19  | 129:128  |            | 2                                                     |     |
|           |          | Health     | greater than 100% in this field after leaving         |     |
manufacturing at the beginning of life.  1% is the
minimum hold up energy required to conduct a proper
shutdown reliably.  A value of 0% may or may not result
in a device failing to shut down properly.  This value shall
never go negative.  Zero is the minimum.

The DSSD Firmware Revision field shall have the
following format:
<Major Revision>.<Minor Revision>.<Release Revision>
where:
• each sub-revision field (i.e., <Major Revision>,
<Minor Revision>, and <Release Revision>) shall
be a base-ten integer in the range 0 to 99,
represented in ASCII;
• the most significant sub-revision field (i.e.,
<Major Revision>) shall be on left;
• each sub-revision field shall be separated by a
period (ASCII 2Eh);
• each sub-revision field of lesser significance shall
reset to “0” (ASCII 30h) when a more significant
sub-revision field increments (e.g., the next
DSSD <Major Revision> release after 1.2.3 would be
SMART-49 277:270 Firmware 8 2.0.0 and the next <Minor Revision> release
Revision after 1.2.3 would be 1.3.0);
• the Firmware Revision field shall not contain
padding of any kind at the start or in the middle
of the string (e.g., zeroes or spaces); and
• if the Firmware Revision field is less than 8
characters, then the Firmware Revision field
shall be padded with spaces at the end of the
string per the NVM Express Base Specification.
Examples of legal values shown inside quotes:
• “1.2.3 ” (3 trailing spaces to make it 8 bytes)
• “10.1.12 ” (1 trailing space to make it 8 bytes)
Examples of illegal values shown inside quotes:
• “1.02.03” (leading zero before 2 and 3 is not
allowed)
• “1. 2. 3” (space before 2 and 3 is not allowed)
• “ 1.2.3” (space at start of string is not allowed)
37

Byte # of
Requirement ID Field Field Description
Address Bytes
• “1.2” (must have all three parts of the revision)
Pre-production firmware shall have a <Major Revision>
of “0”. The first production release of firmware shall
have a <Major Revision> of “1”. The <Major Revision>
shall be incremented by one whenever a major change
is made to the firmware. Examples of major changes
include:
• the Security Firmware Revision is incremented;
• major feature enhancements;
• major architectural changes to the firmware
code base; and
• addition of support for major hardware changes.
The first production release of firmware shall have a
<Minor Revision> of “0”. The <Minor Revision> shall be
incremented by one when only a minor change is made
to the firmware. Examples of minor changes include:
• minor feature enhancements;
• performance enhancements; and
• multiple bug fixes that, in aggregate, justify
more than an increment to the <Release
Revision>.
The <Release Revision> shall be incremented by one for
each firmware revision.
DSSD This field shall contain a UUID in the format specified for
SMART-50 293:278 Firmware 16 UUIDs by the NVM Express Base Specification that is
Build UUID unique for each firmware build.
This field may contain a descriptive label for the
firmware that provides additional information about the
purpose of this revision of the firmware. For example,
this field may be used for test or debug builds to
describe the scope of the build.
DSSD
Examples:
SMART-51 357:294 Firmware 64
• Workaround for issue 12345

• Experimental new feature XYZ

shall be cleared to 0h.

Device hits error The device detects error condition
2
condition
Device saves error related The device saves the following information:
data • Error ID
3 • Device Recovery Actions
• Debug data for the Telemetry Controller-Initiated log page (Log Identifier

Device generates AEN* The device generates the AEN to let the host know that an error was detected
and then starts its error handling workflow. The device is not required to
handle any NVMe command(s) sent via the Admin Submission Queue after
sending the AEN. It is strongly recommended that the device continues to
service commands sent via the out-of-band mechanism, if possible.
The AEN Completion Queue Entry Dword 0 is filled in per DSSD-AEN-1.
If the device is unable to send the AEN to the host (e.g., the Admin CQ is not
usable), and If the device supports the CFS in-band error recovery workflow,
then the device saves the AEN information and asserts CSTS.CFS and starts
4
the CFS-based recovery workflow at step 4.
If the device does not support the CFS-based recovery workflow, then the
host falls back to the recovery functionality specified in the Controller Fatal
Status Condition paragraph of the Error Reporting and Recovery section of
the NVMe Base Specification (i.e., Controller Reset followed by an NVM
Subsystem Reset if the Controller Reset does not recover). If the device
recovers, the device waits for the host to send and AER and then completes
the AEN using the previously saved AEN information and resumes this in-
band error recovery workflow.
5 Host AEN handling The host services the AEN and logs an event for the error condition.
Host waits for device The host waits for Error Reset Wait Time to allow the device to finish its error
6 error handling to handling workflow.
complete

NVMe commands.

8 initialization host will attempt the next Error Reset Action as specified in the Error Reset
Action bitfield.

This vendor-specific log page, C1h shall be 512 bytes with the following functional requirements and field

Bit field indicating potential reset actions that may need
to be taken.  If no reset action is needed, do not set any
of the bits.  More than 1 bit can be set, and it is up to
the host to decide the sequence of action(s) to take.
Instead of asserting and requiring the host to perform
Error Reset

the device should reset itself using a methodology

processing, clear the Processing Paused bit to 0b). The

If autonomous recovery is not possible, then the assert

The strongly preferred order of device advertised
recovery is bit 0, 1, 2, 5, 3 then 4 which is based on least
impactful to most impactful from a host perspective.

The recovery action to take for handling a device error
condition. Value is dependent on the error condition.
The device shall set bit 0 to 1b if data integrity is intact.
The device shall set bit 6 to 1b if the data integrity of
some of the LBAs is compromised. The device shall only
set bit 1, bit 2 or bit 5 to 1b if the data integrity of all of
the LBAs is compromised. The device shall only set bit 3
to 1b or bit 4 to 1b if there is a persistent hardware
failure. The device shall not set more than one bit to

4.8.8  Latency Monitor Log Page and Feature Set Requirements
The following are requirements for the Latency Monitor log page and Latency Monitor Feature Set.  For more
information about the Latency Monitoring Feature Set (see Section 22 Latency Monitoring Feature Set Theory of
Operation).
| Requirement ID  |     |     | Description  |     |
| --------------- | --- | --- | ------------ | --- |
All values in the Latency Monitor log page shall be persistent across power cycles and resets
LMLOG-1
unless otherwise specified.
All counters shall be saturating counters (i.e., if the counter reaches the maximum allowable
LMLOG-2
size, it stops incrementing and does NOT roll back to 0).
LMLOG-3  All values in the Latency Monitor log page shall be little endian format.
A read of the Latency Monitor log page shall be a simple read of the active data and shall
LMLOG-4
not block IO.
Data in the Latency Monitor log page which is read by the host shall be no more than 10
LMLOG-5
minutes old.
When configuring the Latency Monitoring Feature with Set Features the Active Buckets and
LMLOG-6
Static Buckets shall be reset.
46

Requirement ID Description
When powering on, the counters shall run based on the previously configured values. If the
LMLOG-7
values have never been configured, they shall run based on the default values.
The Latency Stamp shall be based on the NVMe timestamp set by the last Timestamp
(Feature 0Eh) Set Features command if any. If a NVMe Timestamp (Feature 0Eh) Set
LMLOG-8
Features command has not been received, then the Latency Stamp shall be based on the
device power on hours.
When the device provides a Latency Stamp of latency outliers, the Latency Stamp shall be
LMLOG-9
based on command completion.
When generating a Latency Monitoring log page (Feature Identifier C5h), the latency shall
be no greater than the latency associated with generating a Telemetry Controller-Initiated
LMLOG-10
log page (Feature Identifier 08h) or a Telemetry Host-Initiated log page (Feature Identifier
07h).
When configuring this feature, the thresholds shall always be configured such that Active
Threshold A < Active Threshold B < Active Threshold C < Active Threshold D. If the host
LMLOG-11
attempts to configure the device in such a way that violates the above rules, the device shall
return Invalid Field in Command.
LMLOG-12 The device shall support the Latency Monitoring Feature Set.
LMLOG-13 The Latency Monitor Log page shall be 512 bytes.
Executing a Set Features command for Latency Monitor log page (Feature Identifier C5h)
LMLOG-14
shall reset all the contents in the Active/Static Buckets.
If the Host Initiated Telemetry Format Supported bit is set to 1b (see LMDATA-1) then the
Latency Monitor Debug Telemetry Log (CAh) shall follow:
LMLOG-15 • The Host-Initiated Telemetry Log Format as defined NVM Express.
• Telemetry Data Area 1, Data Area 2, Data Area 3 and Data Area 4 format as defined
in this specification.
If the Host Initiated Telemetry Format Supported bit is set to 1b (see LMDATA-1) then the
LMLOG-16 Latency Monitor Debug Telemetry Log page (CAh) shall only be cleared with Latency
Monitor Set Features (C5h). See section 4.15.11.
If the Host Initiated Telemetry Format Supported bit is set to 1b, then there shall be no
limits on the size of Data Area 1, 2, 3 or 4 beyond the NVM Express-defined limits. The Data
LMLOG-17
Area size and performance limits in TEL-5 do not apply to the log in the Latency Monitor
Debug Log page (Log Identifier CAh).
If the Host Initiated Telemetry Format Supported bit is set to 1b then the following bytes in
the Latency Monitor Debug log page (Log Identifier CAh) shall be configured as shown:
LMLOG-18 • Byte 00: Log Page Identifier (LID) shall be set to CAh.
• Byte 380: Telemetry Host-Initiated Scope (THS) shall be set to 01h (Controller
Scope).

Bucket Timer reaches the Active Bucket Timer Threshold
then the data specified in Section 22 Latency Monitoring
Feature Set Theory of Operation is moved into the Static
Buckets, the Active Bucket Timer is cleared to 0000h and
restarts counting. If the Active Bucket Timer is running
and there is a power cycle the Active Bucket Timer value
from before the power cycle shall be restored into the
Active Bucket Timer and the Active Bucket Timer shall
continue when the device is powered on.
Active Bucket Timer Threshold is the threshold used to
compare with the Active Bucket Timer. When cleared to
Active Bucket 0000h this threshold is not used, the Active Bucket
LMDATA-4 5:4 Timer 2 Timer will saturate, and the Static Buckets will not be
Threshold loaded. This threshold is in 5-minute increments.
The factory default value of the Active Bucket Timer
Threshold shall be set to 07E0h.
This defines Active Threshold A. This is in 5 ms
Active increments. A value of 00h represents 5 ms. The value
LMDATA-5 6 1
Threshold A FFh represents 1.280 seconds. The factory default is
05h.
Active This is in 5 ms increments. The factory default is 13h.
LMDATA-6 7 1
Threshold B
Active This is in 5 ms increments. The factory default is 1Eh.
LMDATA-7 8 1
Threshold C
Active This is in 5 ms increments. The factory default is 2Eh.
LMDATA-8 9 1
Threshold D
This configures how both the Active Latency Stamp, and
the Active Measured Latency Fields are updated on a
per I/O command (Read, Write, Deallocate) counter
basis.
When the Active Latency Mode is cleared to 0b the
Active Latency Stamp and the Active Measured Latency
Active Latency
LMDATA-9 11:10 2 will trigger and update the first time the associated
Configuration
command counter increments. Once this trigger
happens the fields shall not be updated until the Active
Latency Stamp and Active Measured Latency fields are
reset based on the Active Bucket Timer expiring.

4.8.11 DSSD Power State Requirements
DSSD power states provide an alternative interface to NVMe power management. DSSD and NVMe Power States
are numbered in opposite directions – higher numbered DSSD Power States consume more power than lower
numbered DSSD Power States, whereas higher numbered NVMe Power States consume less power than lower
numbered NVMe Power States.
Selecting a DSSD Power State via a Set Features command (see Section 4.15.15 DSSD Power State (Feature
Identifier C7h) Set Feature) causes the device to run at the highest powered NVMe Power State whose Maximum
Power (MP) in watts is less than or equal to the number of the DSSD Power State. For example, placing the
device in DSSD Power State number 20 causes the device to enter the highest powered NVMe Power State
whose Maximum Power (MP) is less than or equal to 20 watts.
In general, a device will have more DSSD Power States than NVMe Power States. Selecting a DSSD Power State
whose number is not the Maximum Power (MP) in watts of an NVMe Power State causes the device to drop
down to run at the highest powered NVMe Power State whose Maximum Power (MP) does not exceed the
number of the DSSD Power State in watts.
65

For example, suppose that a device supports NVMe Power State 5 that consumes no more than 20 watts
Maximum Power (MP) and NVMe Power State 6 that consumes no more than 16 watts Maximum Power (MP).
Selecting DSSD Power State 18 (i.e., 18 watts Maximum Power (MP)) causes the device to enter NVMe Power
State 6 and consume no more than 16 watts Maximum Power (MP).  In this example the device reports 18 as its
DSSD Power State and 6 as its NVMe Power State.  Selecting NVMe Power State 6 causes the device to report 16
as its DSSD Power State and 6 as its NVMe Power State.
DSSD Power State 0 does not exist, as a device that is consuming 0 watts Maximum Power (MP) is powered off.
DSSD Power States that represent a Maximum Power (MP) less than the lowest powered NVMe Power State are
invalid.  The lowest numbered valid DSSD Power State is indicated in DCLP-8.
| 4.8.11.1  DSSD Power State Descriptor  |     |     |     |     |
| -------------------------------------- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
The DSSD Power State Descriptor for each DSSD Power State has the following format:
| Requirement ID  | Bits  | Field  |     | Field Description  |
| --------------- | ----- | ------ | --- | ------------------ |

State
to the number of this DSSD Power State.

4.8.13  Hardware Component Log Page (Log Identifier C6h) Requirements
This log page provides the host with information regarding the hardware components on the device.  This log
page is intended to enable customers to be able to parse this log when there are component issues to be able to
find failing devices.  This also enables customers to be able to parse this log for failing devices and not require
device serial numbers to find the devices with component issues.
Requirement ID  Description
HWCOMP-1  A value of zero shall only be used if the corresponding component data is not available.

HWCOMP-3
hardware components.

4.8.14  TCG Configuration Log Page (Log Identifier C7h) Requirements
TCG Configuration Log shall be 512 bytes in size.  This log defines the data points related to TCG Opal Security
Subsystem Class (SSC) that would be useful to collect for diagnostic purposes.  These data points give point-in-
time insight into the configuration and state of the device which can be used to explain either a device or host
behavior.
| TCG Log Behavior Type  |     |     |     | Persistence Type  |     |     |     |
| ---------------------- | --- | --- | --- | ----------------- | --- | --- | --- |
A   Persistent across TCG revert: PSID, Admin SP, Locking SP
B   Not persistent across TCG revert

TCG Log
|                 | Byte     |        | # of   |                    |     | Behavior  |           |
| --------------- | -------- | ------ | ------ | ------------------ | --- | --------- | --------- |
| Requirement ID  |          | Field  |        | Field Description  |     |           | Behavior  |
|                 | Address  |        | Bytes  |                    |     | Type      |           |
Type

4.8.15  Telemetry String Log Page (Log Identifier C9h) Requirements
The Telemetry String log page enables mapping of Statistic Identifiers, Debug Class/Event Identifiers and Debug
Class/VU Event Identifier combinations to ASCII strings.
| 4.8.15.1  Telemetry String Log Page Requirements  |     |     |     |              |     |     |
| ------------------------------------------------- | --- | --- | --- | ------------ | --- | --- |
| Requirement ID                                    |     |     |     | Description  |     |     |
All Statistic Identifiers contained in Data Area 1 and Data Area 2 shall be contained in this log
TELSLG-1
page.
String Identifier Table entries shall be in numeric order such that the smallest Vendor
TELSLG-2
Unique Statistic Identifier is at the lowest address.
All Debug Event Class/ Event Identifier combinations contained in Telemetry Data Area 1 and
TELSLG-3
Telemetry Data Area 2 shall be contained in this log page.
All Debug Event Class/ VU Event Identifier combinations contained in Telemetry Data Area 1
TELSLG-4
and Telemetry Data Area 2 shall be contained in this log page.
String Event Table entries shall be in numeric order such that the smallest Debug event Class
TELSLG-5
is at the lowest address.
String VU Event Table entries shall be in numeric order such that the smallest Debug event
TELSLG-6
Class is at the lowest address.
String Event Table entries shall be in numeric order such that for a single Debug/Event
TELSLG-7
Identifier combination the smallest Event Identifier is at the lowest address.
String VU Event Table entries shall be in numeric order such that for a single Debug/VU
TELSLG-8
Event Identifier combination the smallest VU Event Identifier is at the lowest address.
74

Requirement ID  Description
In the ASCII table (See Section 4.8.15.2 Telemetry String Log Page Format), characters which
TELSLG-9
are not valid (beyond the length of the ASCII length) shall be set to <space> (i.e., 20h).
TELSLG-10  The String Identifier Table shall have no gaps between this table and the String Event Table.
The String Event Table entry shall have no gaps between this table and the VU String Event
TELSLG-11
Table.
TELSLG-12  The VU String Event Table and the ASCII table shall have no gaps between these tables.
The String Identifier Table Entries, The String Event Table Entries and the String VU Event
TELSLG-13
Table Entries may point to the same ASCII Table Entry.
Statistic Identifiers (see Section 4.9.11 Statistics Identifiers) which are not vendor unique
and Debug / Event Identifiers (see Section 4.9.15.2 Event Classes) which are not vendor
TELSLG-14  unique and are defined by this specification are not required to be populated in the String
Log if the OCP plugin for the nvme-cli tool is able to decode these due to the decodes being
populated in the tool.  This is an exception to TELSLG-1 and TELSLG-3.
| 4.8.15.2  Telemetry String Log Page Format  |     |     |     |     |

An ASCII ID Length/Decode example is shown in the following table:
|     | Byte  |     | Data Byte  |     | ASCII Character  |
| --- | ----- | --- | ---------- | --- | ---------------- |
|     | 400   |     | 54h        |     | T                |
|     | 401   |     | 45h        |     | E                |
|     | 402   |     | 53h        |     | S                |
|     | 403   |     | 54h        |     | T                |
|     | 404   |     | 20h        |     | <space>          |
|     | 405   |     | 45h        |     | E                |
|     | 406   |     | 58h        |     | X                |
|     | 407   |     | 41h        |     | A                |
|     | 408   |     | 4Dh        |     | M                |
|     | 409   |     | 50h        |     | P                |
|     | 410   |     | 4Ch        |     | L                |
|     | 411   |     | 45h        |     | E                |
|     | 412   |     | 21h        |     | !                |
|     | 413   |     | 20h        |     | <space>          |
|     | 414   |     | 20h        |     | <space>          |
|     | 415   |     | 20h        |     | <space>          |
 In this example the ASCII ID Length is 0Ch, which is 12 decimal.  This is a zero-based count and thus there are 13
characters to print.  The first 13 characters shall be part of the ASCII output.  Thus, the message to print is:
 “TEST EXAMPLE!”
80

The last three ASCII <space> characters are not part of the ASCII output. They are only used for padding the
string to the next Dword boundary. The last three ASCII characters of <space> are not part of the next string.
4.9 Host and Controller Initiated Telemetry Log Pages
The following requirements define a standardized format for Telemetry Data Area 1 and Telemetry Data Area 2
for both Telemetry Host-Initiated log page (Log Identifier 07h) and Telemetry Controller-Initiated log page (Log
Identifier 08h).
4.9.1 Theory of Operation
This feature is designed to enable both customers and vendors to have increased visibility into monitoring and
debugging devices.
4.9.2 Data Partitioning Overview
The data provided by the device for debugging is broken into two categories. There is data that impacts I/O and
data that does not impact I/O. The data generated by the device for monitoring and/or debugging which does
not impact I/O (performance/latency) for active commands in progress goes into Telemetry Data Area 1. The
data generated by the device for monitoring and/or debugging which impacts I/O (performance/latency) for
active commands in progress goes into Telemetry Data Area 2. The data format in the Telemetry Host-Initiated
log page and the Telemetry Controller-Initiated log page shall be the same format (see Section 4.6.16.1
Telemetry Data Format).
The information (i.e., statistics and events) reported in Telemetry Host-Initiated Data Areas 1 and 2 shall be the
same as Telemetry Controller-Initiated Data Areas 1 and 2. There is no requirement that the data contents of
Telemetry Host-Initiated Data Areas 1 and 2 be the same as the data contents of Telemetry Controller-Initiated
Data Areas 1 and 2 because each log page is captured by different events, and each log page reports current data
(e.g., counts of commands processed) at the time of capture. In addition, the order of statistic descriptors (see
Section 4.9.10 Statistic Descriptor) and the order of event descriptors (see Section 4.9.14.1 Event Descriptor) are
both allowed to differ between the two log pages.
4.9.3 Statistic Area
The Statistic Area contains a group of Statistic Descriptors. The Statistic Descriptors may be counters or other
statistics where each statistic is a value with a statistic size. The attributes associated with each of these statistics
are Statistic Identifier, Behavior Type (see STD-LOG-12) and the length of the data field associated with the
Statistic Identifier.
4.9.4 Event FIFO
The Event FIFO is a queue that contains events that are generated. There is a total of up to 16 independent
Event FIFO queues that may be configured between Telemetry Data Area 1 and Telemetry Data Area 2. It should
be noted that the ordering relationship of events in the event FIFO is determined by the device.
4.9.5 Existing NVMe Log Pages
There are many existing NVMe log pages that are useful for monitoring the device. Some log pages have been
overlaid into Telemetry Data Area 1 (see TEL-23). This is done to enable all the monitoring information to be
gathered when polling Telemetry Data Area 1.
81

4.9.6 Debug Structure Overview Summary
The debug structure for Telemetry Data Area 1 and 2 can be seen in the following figure. The order of the
Statistics and FIFOs are configurable, and both orders are acceptable.

TEL-26

Support feature before requesting data from Telemetry Data Area 4.

4.9.9 Debug Profiles
There are many ways to configure Data Area 1, Data Area 2, the Statistics and Event FIFOs. Depending on the
problem being investigated different configurations of these fields may be desired. Debug profiles are the
mechanism that can address this challenge. The device will list the number of debug profiles supported. The
host may then configure the profile based on the problem being investigated.

4.9.12  Context Statistic Descriptor
Context Statistic Descriptors encapsulate other Statistic Descriptors and provide additional context information
about the source of the data.  The Statistic Identifier value defines the type of context provided by the Context
Statistic Descriptor, and the Context Value field(s) define the specific context for the encapsulated data.  Statistic
Descriptors for namespaces should continue to use the NSID field unless the identifier exceeds the 16-bit field
limit of the NSID field.
| 4.9.12.1  Context Statistic Descriptor Requirements  |     |     |     |              |     |     |
| ---------------------------------------------------- | --- | --- | --- | ------------ | --- | --- |
| Requirement ID                                       |     |     |     | Description  |     |     |
The first Dword of the Statistic Specific Data field (see STATF-6) shall contain the number of
Dwords in the Context Data and shall be greater than zero.  The Context Data includes the
STAT-CSD-1
Context Data Size field and the Context Data Fields, as shown in the Context Statistic
Descriptor Layout Figure.
The size and format of the Context Data in a Context Statistic Descriptor are determined by
STAT-CSD-2  the Statistic Identifier value.  Context Data Fields are defined for each context type in Section
4.9.12.2 Context Types.
Encapsulated Statistic Descriptors within a Context Statistic Descriptor shall not include any
STAT-CSD-3
Context Statistic Descriptors.
The Namespace Information field (see STATF-3) and Namespace Identifier[15:0] field (see
STAT-CSD-4  STATF-5) in a Context Statistic Descriptor shall be cleared to 0h.  Encapsulated Statistic
Descriptors are able to use the Namespace Information and Namespace Identifier fields.
98

| 4.9.12.2  Context Types  |     |     |     |     |
| ------------------------ | --- | --- | --- | --- |
This section defines the Index Context types that can be used to provide context information for Statistic
Descriptors.  These data structures follow the 2-Dword header for all Statistic Descriptors (see Section 4.9.10
Statistic Descriptor).
| 4.9.12.2.1  Namespace ID Context (Statistic Identifier 6Dh)  |          |        |        |                    |
| ------------------------------------------------------------ | -------- | ------ | ------ | ------------------ |
|                                                              | Byte     |        | # of   |                    |
| Requirement ID                                               |          | Field  |        | Field Description  |
|                                                              | Address  |        | Bytes  |                    |
The number of Dwords in the context data, including
Context Data
this field.

4.9.14  Statistic Requirements
Requirement ID  Description
SDL-1  Statistic Area 1 shall not cross from Telemetry Data Area 1 to Telemetry Data Area 2.
SDL-2  Bytes in the Statistics Areas that are not contained in a Statistic Descriptor shall be zero.
The decode of the Statistic Identifiers shall be provided to the customer via the Telemetry
SDL-3
String log page.

4.9.15.2  Event Classes
This section defines the Event Class information that can be used to debug issues with the device.
4.9.15.2.1  Debug Event Class Types
Debug Event Class Code  Description
00h  Reserved
01h  Timestamp Debug Class

115

# of

| EVC-VF-1        | 0        |               | 1                     |                    |
Class
Virtual FIFO Event Identifier:
Event ID   Description
|           |      | Virtual FIFO  | 0000h  | Virtual FIFO Start.  |
| --------- | ---- | ------------- | ------ | -------------------- |
| EVC-VF-2  | 2:1  |               | 2      |                      |
|           |      | Identifier    | 0001h  | Virtual FIFO End.    |
0002- Reserved.
FFFFh

|           |     | Virtual FIFO  | This shall be set to 1h.  |     |
| --------- | --- | ------------- | ------------------------- | --- |
| EVC-VF-3  | 3   |               | 1                         |     |
Data Size
This is the required format of the VU Virtual FIFO
Identifier.
Bit   VU Virtual FIFO Identifier Bit Description
This is the physical Event FIFO Number.   Valid
|           |                  | VU Virtual  |           | values are 1h to 10h.   A value of 0h is not  |
| --------- | ---------------- | ----------- | --------- | --------------------------------------------- |
| EVC-VF-4  | 5:4              |             | 2  15:11  |                                               |
|           | FIFO Identifier  |             |           | valid.  An example physical event FIFO is     |
TELDF-18 is event FIFO 1.
This is the virtual FIFO number within the
10:0  physical FIFO.
Note:   Bits 7:0 are the LSB which is in byte 4.

| EVC-VF-5  | 7:6  | Reserved  | 2  This shall be set to 0h.  |     |
| --------- | ---- | --------- | ---------------------------- | --- |
This indicates the start/end of a virtual FIFO within a physical FIFO.   The name of the virtual FIFO can be found in
the String Log using the VU Virtual FIFO Identifier.

4.9.16 Event FIFO Location
The Event FIFO X location in Telemetry Data Area 1 can be found by using the Event FIFO X Start, Event FIFO X
Size. This can be seen in the following Telemetry Data Area 1 Event FIFO Figure:
The Event FIFO location in Telemetry Data Area 2 can be found by using the Event FIFO X Start, Event FIFO X Data
End. This can be seen in the following Telemetry Data Area 2 Event FIFO Figure:
121

4.9.16.1 Event FIFO Requirements
Requirement ID Description
EVF-1 The oldest event descriptor shall be at the Event FIFO Start Address.
EVF-2 There shall be no gaps between the data in one descriptor and the next descriptor.
EVF-3 The event FIFO shall only have complete descriptors (i.e., no partial descriptors).
All data contained in the event FIFO that is not contained in an event descriptor shall be
EVF-4
cleared to zero.
For a single FIFO, the Event FIFO Start and Event FIFO End shall be in the same Telemetry
EVF-5
Data Area.
EVF-6 Event FIFO Start and End locations shall not overlap with the Statistic Descriptor locations.
The decode of the Event Class and Vendor Unique Event Class shall be provided to the
EVF-7
customer via the Telemetry String log page.
4.9.17 Telemetry Data Area

4.10 Device Self-test Requirements
To normalize the reporting of Device Self-test data, the following Segment Numbers are defined.

The device shall use the following segment numbers:
|     | Segment  |               | Test Performed  |      | Failure Criteria  |
