A short device self-test operation (i.e., the STC field is set to 1h) shall complete in less than
SELFTST-2
or equal to 2 minutes.
An extended device self-test operation (i.e., the STC field is set to 2h) shall complete in less
SELFTST-3 than or equal to 30 minutes (i.e., the EDSTT field shall indicate a value of less than or equal
to 30 minutes).
A vendor-specific self-test operation (i.e., the STC field is set to Eh) shall complete the test
SELFTST-4
specified by SELFTST-7 in less than or equal to 2 seconds.
A device self-test operation shall not fail if it is unable to complete within the specified
completion time (e.g., due to
SELFTST-5
concurrent host I/O activity). The device shall complete
as many device self-test segments as possible within the allotted completion time.
For a Self-test Code (STC) of 2h, the device self-test operation shall terminate upon reading
SELFTST-6
all allocated LBAs and completing all non-media related tests.
For a Device Self-test Code (STC) of 1h or Eh, the device self-test operation shall include at a
minimum,
SELFTST-7
segments 1 to 3 and 8, and as much as possible of segments 4 to 7, within the completion
time specified for that specific operation.
SELFTST-8 Obsolete. See SELFTST-1 segments 2 and 10.
The device vendor shall provide the minimum number of LBAs required to be written
by the host to enable the extended device self-test operation to read from all physical non-
SELFTST-9
volatile memory elements (e.g., NAND die). A segment shall not fail solely due to the host
writing less than the minimum number of LBAs.
If the Device Self-test command is reissued after a previous Device Self-test command and
operation
different LBAs
SELFTST-10
allocated LBAs, but only
Self-test completion time, then the first run of
the Device Self-test would scan LBAs 0h to 5FFFh, the next run would scan LBAs 6000h to
132

Requirement ID Description
BFFFh and the
1FFFh, and so forth.
The device self-test operation shall not be destructive to any user data (note that reading
user data once during the device self-test operation is not considered destructive, because
SELFTST-11
even though it technically causes read disturb,
the effect is minimal).
4.11 Firmware Update Requirements
This defines the requirements for firmware update in the device.
Requirement ID Description
FWUP-1 Obsolete. See STD-LOG-10.
Other than media end-of-life, devices shall not have any restrictions on the number of
FWUP-2
firmware downloads supported.
The Firmware Commit command with the following Commit Action (CA) codes shall be
supported:
• 000b – Download only.
FWUP-3
• 001b – Download and activate upon reset.
• 010b – Activate upon reset.
• 011b – Activate immediately without reset.
Firmware Image Download command shall be supported and shall not cause any
FWUP-4
performance impact.
FWUP-5 Obsolete.
The device shall support a minimum of 2 read/write slots for firmware update and may
FWUP-6
support up to 7.
The controller shall set the Maximum Time for Firmware Activation (MTFA) field to a value
FWUP-7 that is less than or equal to Ah (1s). This time limit applies only to Commit Action 011b
(firmware activation without reset) of the Firmware Commit command, see FWUP-30.
If a Firmware Commit command is processed that specifies a firmware image that has a
Security Firmware Revision (see SMART-22) that is less than the Security Firmware Revision
FWUP-8 of the currently running firmware image, then the device shall abort that Firmware Commit
command with a status code of Firmware Activation Prohibited (13h).
See SEC-3 for additional firmware anti-rollback requirements.
The firmware image in each valid firmware slot shall have multiple copies of that firmware
FWUP-9 image on separate physical non-volatile memory devices (e.g., NAND die, NAND RAID stripe)
for reliability.
Firmware activation shall not cause or require data (e.g., user data, log page contents, etc.)
FWUP-10
to be lost or destroyed.
FWUP-11 Firmware activation without reset shall occur seamlessly on a running system:
133

Requirement ID Description
• The device shall preserve the current state of the device (e.g., Opal locking state,
current value of each Feature, Timestamp, I/O Submission/Completion Queue
setup, NVMe-MI state such as MCTP Transmission Unit Size, SMBus/I2C/I3C
Frequency, and MCTP state such as the MCTP endpoint ID, LBA format, PCIe state,
etc.).
• The PCIe link state shall not be impacted.
The firmware image shall contain the firmware for all the device’s controllers (NVMe
FWUP-12
controllers, management controllers, etc.).
The VPD/FRU Data shall be a part of the device’s firmware update image and shall be field
upgradable using the standard NVMe Firmware Image Download/Firmware Commit
FWUP-13
commands. VPD fields that are unique to the device (e.g., Serial Number) shall be
preserved during a firmware update.
The size of the firmware shall be 6 MiB or less in order to facilitate firmware update via low-
FWUP-14
bandwidth interfaces (e.g., NVMe-MI over SMBus).
Requiring a reset of any type to activate firmware under any condition shall be avoided. If a
reset is unavoidable, the device vendor shall request a waiver from the end customer. In
FWUP-15
cases where waivers are granted, a Controller Level Reset is preferred over a Conventional
Reset. Firmware Activation requiring an NVMe Subsystem Reset should always be avoided.
All firmware updates shall be allowed to be performed by the system vendor or end user
without any outside assistance from NVMe device vendor employees or anyone else and
FWUP-16 shall not require any additional vendor-specific actions or equipment (such as dongles,
debug cables, etc.) unless otherwise noted in this specification. This includes both pre-
production and production firmware.
Firmware updates shall not require an intermediate firmware update or "bridge code" to
update from one firmware version to the next subsequent version (e.g., N-1 firmware
FWUP-17
revision to bridge firmware to N firmware is prohibited). This includes both pre-production
and production firmware.
The device shall not be left in an unusable state due to any reset or loss of power during a
firmware update. Depending on where in the device’s firmware activation process the reset
or loss of power occurs, the device shall either:
FWUP-18
• abort the firmware activation and continue running with the firmware revision that
was running at the start of the firmware update process; or
• complete the firmware activation and start running with the new firmware revision.
For production-level firmware, all means of updating the firmware besides the Firmware
FWUP-19 Image Download/Firmware Commit commands (e.g., via MMIO or any vendor-proprietary
mechanisms) shall be disabled.
The device shall support a read-only firmware slot (slot 1). If a firmware image is
FWUP-20 successfully activated to a read-write slot that increases the Security Version Number (see
SMART-22), then the device shall also update the read-only slot 1 with that firmware image.
134

Requirement ID Description
If the Firmware Slot field in the Firmware Commit command is cleared to 0h, then the
FWUP-21 device shall commit the firmware image to a firmware slot that does not contain the
currently running firmware image.
If the current active firmware image is corrupt, then the device shall automatically fail over
to another backup copy of that firmware image until all backup copies of that firmware
FWUP-22 image are exhausted. The device shall not automatically fail over to another revision of
firmware in a different firmware slot; this overrides the NVM Express Base Specification.
The vendor should follow the guidelines in NIST SP 800-193.
A single firmware image shall cover all the devices in a product family. For example, devices
with the same model but different capacity points, endurance or form factor shall have one
firmware image that works on all devices. A single firmware image shall cover all TCG Opal
capable and non-TCG Opal capable devices in a given product family.
An exception is that the firmware for a family of FIPS 140-3 compliant devices is different
than the firmware for the same family of non-FIPS 140-3 compliant devices. In particular,
FWUP-23
the firmware for the family of FIPS 140-3 compliant devices shall contain the FIPS 140
compliance descriptor (see SEC-52) whereas the firmware for the family of non-FIPS 140-3
compliant devices shall not contain the FIPS 140 compliance descriptor. Other than the FIPS
140 compliance descriptor, the firmware for the family of FIPS 140-3 compliant devices
should be the same as the firmware for the same family of non-FIPS 140-3 compliant
devices.
Every firmware image shall have a firmware signature that meets the requirements of SBT-1
and SBT-4. The device shall check the firmware signature as part of processing any
FWUP-24 Firmware Commit command that commits a firmware image to a firmware slot. If the
firmware signature check fails, the device shall abort the Firmware Commit command with
Invalid Firmware Image status.
If a Firmware Commit command activates a firmware image from the same firmware slot as
the currently running firmware image (where the currently running firmware image is the
firmware that processed the Firmware Commit command), then:
• the device shall keep a copy of the currently running firmware image until the newly
activated firmware image completes initialization successfully at least once; and
FWUP-25 • if the firmware image that is being activated is unable to complete initialization
successfully for any reason, then the device shall revert to the firmware that
processed the Firmware Commit command; and
• once the newly activated firmware image successfully completes initialization at
least once, the firmware image for the firmware that processed the Firmware
Commit command is permitted to be discarded.
For a successful Firmware Commit command with Commit Action 001b or 010b (firmware is
activated at the next Controller Level Reset) and for a Firmware Commit command with
FWUP-26 Commit Action 011b (activate firmware without reset) that is aborted with Firmware
Activation Requires Controller Level Reset status, the device shall complete the firmware
activation process within 5 seconds from the start of the Controller Level Reset.
135

Requirement ID Description
For an active slot firmware update, upon completing the firmware activate of the new
firmware, the firmware slot shall only contain multiple copies of the active firmware with no
FWUP-27 other additional information. When updating a firmware slot which is not active, upon
completing the Firmware Commit command, the firmware slot being updated shall only
contain multiple copies of the committed firmware with no other additional information.
For a FIPS 140-3 device:
• if the Cryptographic Module Boundary encompasses the entire physical device, then
the Firmware Version value(s) in the FIPS 140-3 certification shall match the value(s)
indicated by the Firmware Revision field in the Identify Controller data structure;
and
FWUP-28 • if the Cryptographic Module Boundary does not encompass the entire physical
device, then there is no requirement that the Firmware Version value(s) in the FIPS
140-3 certification match the value(s) indicated by the Firmware Revision field in the
Identify Controller data structure. SEC-47 strongly recommends that the
Cryptographic Module Boundary not encompass the entire physical device.
All FIPS 140-3 devices are required to provide FIPS 140 compliance information, see SEC-52.
The device shall set the Firmware Update Granularity (FWUG) field to 01h indicating and
FWUP-29
firmware update granularity of 4,096 bytes.
For a Firmware Commit command with Commit Action 011b (firmware activation without
FWUP-30 reset), the device shall complete the firmware activation process within MTFA seconds after
submission of the Firmware Commit command to an empty Admin Queue, see FWUP-7.
The device shall be ready to accept host I/O and NVMe Admin commands upon completion
FWUP-31
of the Firmware Commit Command.
The device shall reject any attempt to commit or activate any firmware image that is not
appropriate for the device (e.g., a firmware image for a FIPS 140-3 compliant device may or
may not be appropriate for a device that is not FIPS 140-3 compliant, see FWUP-23).
Rejection of a firmware image shall neither render the device inoperable nor impair device
FWUP-32 functionality.
The means of firmware image rejection is device-specific, e.g., if different keys are used to
sign firmware images for different devices, then attempting to commit or activate an
inappropriate firmware image fails because the device is unable to validate the firmware
image signature.
4.12 Factory Default Requirements
This section defines additional requirements for the state of the device as shipped from the factory. In addition
to the factory default requirements in this section, factory default requirements listed in other sections of this
document are also required (e.g., NVMe-AD-22).
Requirement ID Description
FDEF-1 All firmware slots shall contain the most recent production firmware revision.
FDEF-2 All logical blocks shall be deallocated.
136

Requirement ID Description
The following SMART / Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h) fields shall be
cleared to 0h: Critical Warning, Endurance Group Critical Warning Summary, Data Units
FDEF-3 Read, Data Units Written, Host Read Commands, Host Write Commands, Controller Busy
Time, Power Cycles, Power On Hours, Unsafe Shutdowns, Media, and Data Integrity Errors,
Percentage Used, and Number of Error Information Log Entries.
The Available Spare field in the SMART / Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h)
FDEF-4
shall be set to a value of 100.
The Total Number of Events field in the Persistent Event log page (Log Identifier 0Dh) shall
FDEF-5
be cleared to 0h.
All features that are saveable shall not have a saved value unless otherwise specified. This
FDEF-6
requirement applies to features in the NVM Express Specifications and this specification.
4.13 Deallocation Requirements
Requirement ID Description
TRIM-1 The device shall support the Deallocate attribute of the Dataset Management command.
Once the device has deallocated a logical block, a read of that logical block shall return all
bytes cleared to 0h until that logical block has been modified by a command (e.g., Write,
TRIM-2
Copy, etc.) (i.e., bits 2:0 = 001b in the Deallocate Logical Block Features (DLFEAT) field in the
Identify Namespace data structure).
TRIM-3 Obsolete (see TRIM-2).
Device deallocated logical blocks shall provide the performance and reliability benefits of
TRIM-4
overprovisioned space.
TRIM-5 The device shall support Garbage Collection during periods of no I/O (Idle GC).
Processing of deallocation requested by a Dataset Management command shall not cause
TRIM-6 read latency for LBAs that are outside the LBA ranges being deallocated to change by more
than 5% from baseline.
If Read I/O occurs while Idle GC is active, then Read latency shall not increase more than 5%
TRIM-7
from baseline.
If any device deallocated logical blocks have been subsequently read or written to, then the
TRIM-8 contents of those logical blocks shall not change as a consequence of an unsafe power down
event.
The device shall deallocate data to the maximum extent possible provided that it does not
TRIM-9 violate TRIM-6 or TRIM-7. Background deallocate processing is allowed provided that it
does not violate TRIM-8.
137

4.14 Sector Size and Namespace Support
Requirement ID Description
SECTOR-1 Obsolete. Replaced by SECTOR-4.
SECTOR-2 Obsolete. Replaced by SECTOR-4.
A new device shipped from the factory shall have one active Namespace whose size in bytes
SECTOR-3 and capacity in bytes are the same and consume the maximum capacity that is listed on the
device label (see SECTOR-5).
SECTOR-4 The device shall support 512-byte and 4096-byte logical block sizes.
The capacity listed on the device label (see the capacity row in LABL-1) and the maximum
number of logical blocks that the device is able to allocate to a single namespace (i.e., the
maximum possible value of NCAP) shall comply with the latest revision of the SFF-8447
SECTOR-5 Specification for LBA Count for Disk Drives:
• for all form factors, including form factors not explicitly listed in the SFF-8447
Specification; and
• for all LBA Formats supported by the device.
A device that has 128TB raw NAND capacity shall list a capacity of 122.88 TB or greater on
the device label. A device that has 256TB raw NAND capacity shall list a capacity of 245.76
SECTOR-6 TB or greater on the device label.
Some devices are required to list exactly 122.88 TB capacity or exactly 245.76 TB capacity on
the device label, i.e., listing a greater capacity is prohibited, see DP-CFG-12.
4.15 Set/Get Features Requirements
This section describes features defined by this specification. Unless otherwise specified, the device shall support
all the features defined in this section.
4.15.1 General Feature Requirements
Requirement ID Description
For any Feature Identifier defined in this section, Selection (SEL) values 00b to 11b in Dword
GETF-1
10 of the Get Features command shall be supported.
If the feature requested by Set Features or by Get Features is not supported, then a status
GETF-2
error code of 02h (Invalid Field in Command) shall be returned.
GETF-3 The device shall not implement a Feature with Feature Identifier D0h.
For any Feature Identifier defined in this section that is not Namespace scoped, the host
should either clear the Namespace Identifier (NSID) field in the Get Features command to
GETF-4 zero or set that field to FFFFFFFFh. In addition, the host may set that field to a valid NSID if
the feature is Namespace scoped. The device shall return the appropriate status based on
the NVM Express Specifications.
138

Requirement ID  Description
If the SEL field is set to 11b (i.e., Supported Features) in a Get Features command for any
Feature Identifier defined in this section, then the following capabilities for that Feature
Identifier shall be returned in CQE Dword 0:
| Bit  | Bit Name            | Bit Value  |
| ---- | ------------------- | ---------- |
| 7:3  | Reserved            | 0b         |
| 2    | Changeable (CHANG)  | 1b         |
GETF-5
| 1   | NS Specific (NSSPEC)  | See below  |
| --- | --------------------- | ---------- |
| 0   | Saveable (SVBL)       | See below  |
If the scope of the Feature (see Section 4.15.2 DSSD Feature Requirements) is Namespace,
then the NSSPEC bit shall be set to 1b, otherwise, the NSSPEC bit shall be cleared to 0b.
If the Feature is saveable (see Section 4.15.2 DSSD Feature Requirements), then the SVBL bit
shall be set to 1b, otherwise the SVBL bit shall be cleared to 0b.

Scope KEY:
•  Namespace = The Set Feature affects a specific namespace.
•  Controller = The Set Feature affects the controller that is processing the command.
•
NVM subsystem = The Set Feature affects the NVM subsystem.
Persistence KEY:
•  Yes = Current setting persists across power cycles and resets, and the Feature is not saveable.
•  No = Current setting does not persist across power cycles and resets, and the Feature is not saveable.
•  Saveable = Current setting does not persist across power cycles and resets, and the Feature is
saveable.
The device shall support the following additional vendor unique Set/Get Features Identifiers.
4.15.3  Event Injection (Feature Identifier C0h) Set Features
Feature to inject an event to be simulated and reported by the device for the purpose of exercising the event
behavior or error handling and recovery functionality in the device and the host.  For injected errors, the device
is not required to actually undergo the injected error (e.g. perform an unsafe shutdown or corrupt the FTL), but
the device is required to behave as if the injected error has occurred.
If multiple Set Features commands for this feature are sent by the host, then only information from the most
recent successful command is retained (i.e., subsequent commands replace information provided by previous
commands).

Requirement ID Description
ERRI-1 The number of entries in the Number of Event Injections field shall be 1.
A value of 0000000b in the Number of Event Injections field shall clear the untriggered
ERRI-2
event injection, if any.
ERRI-3 Obsolete.
The host shall clear any unused entries in the Event Injection data structure to zero and the
ERRI-4 device shall ignore all zeroed entries. The device shall check at least the first four bytes of
each Event Injection Entry data structure to determine if it is zeroed.
The device shall abort the Event Injection Set Features command if the request contains an
ERRI-5
event injection type that is not supported.
Once the trigger conditions specified in an Event Injection Entry are met, the device shall
inject the defined error event such that the host can detect the error through device
behavior, e.g., an AEN being sent, the CFS bit being set, delayed receipt of command
ERRI-6 completion, or command being aborted. The device is not required to cause the injected
error to occur (e.g., injecting an Incomplete Shutdown error requires the device to behave
as if an Incomplete Shutdown occurred, but does not require the device to perform an
Incomplete Shutdown).
ERRI-7 Obsolete.
The device shall clear the triggered event, if any, at the next power cycle (i.e., next power
cycle reverts device behavior to have no injected event) unless otherwise specified for a
ERRI-8
specific injected event in Section 4.15.3.3 Event Definition Table (e.g., see the definition of
Recovery Type 4 in EVTREC-4).

4.15.4 Event Injection (Feature Identifier C0h) Get Features
This Get Features returns the event injection that is enabled on the device if any, GETF-4 specifies the acceptable
values of the NSID field in the Get Features command. The attributes specified in Section 4.15.3.4 - Device Event
Injection Type are returned in Dword 0 of the completion queue entry and the Event Injection data structure
specified in Section 4.15.3.1 - Event Injection Entry Data Structure is returned for the event injection in the data
buffer for that command. If there are no currently enabled event injections, the data buffer returned shall
contain all zeroes. The device shall clear to zero all unused entries in the Event Injection data structure.
4.15.4.1 Event Injection – Get Features Completion Queue Entry Dword 0
Requirement ID Field Bits Field Description
GERRI-1 Reserved 31:7 Shall be cleared to zero.
The returned value depends on the contents of the Select (SEL)
field in the Get Features command.
Current value (Select (SEL) field cleared to 000b): This field
indicates if there is an untriggered event injection. If so,
information about that outstanding event injection is returned in
Number of the command data buffer (see Section 4.15.3.1 Event Injection
Event Entry Data Structure for the format of the entry).
GERRI-2 6:0
Injections
(NUME) Default value (Select (SEL) field set to 001b) or saved value
(Selection (SEL) set to 010b): This field shall be cleared to 00h.
This feature is not saveable (see SERRI-10), so a request for the
saved value returns the default value.
Capabilities (Select (SEL) field set to 011b): See GETF-5.

The device shall default from the factory to Read Only Mode (ROM) (01b). This requirement
ROWTM-1 applies regardless of whether the PLP Failure Mode feature is enabled or disabled (see DP-
CFG-6).

4.15.8  Clear PCIe Correctable Error Counters (Feature Identifier C3h) Get Features
A Get Features command for Feature Identifier C3h should not be issued because no useful information is
returned.  GETF-4 specifies the acceptable values of the NSID field in a Get Features command.
Requirement ID  Description
The returned value depends on the value of the Select (SEL) field in the Get Features
command.
If the Select (SEL) field is cleared to 000b (current value), set to 001b (default value), or set
GPCIE-1  to 010b (saved value), then the device shall clear Dword 0 of the completion queue entry to
zero.  This feature is not saveable (see CPCIE-10), so a request for the saved value returns
the default value.
If the Select (SEL) field is set to 011b (i.e., Capabilities), see GETF-5.

|                 | Byte     |        | # of   |                    |

| LMDS-8  | 10:9  |                 | 2        |     |
| ------- | ----- | --------------- | -------- | --- |

Value  Description
When cleared to 00h the debug log, if it
00h
exists, will not be cleared.
When set to 01h the debug log will be
discarded so another log can be triggered.
In addition to this, all the fields in the Set
Features Data structure are valid, which will
cause the Latency Monitor feature to be
01h
reset and loaded with the values from the
Set Features command.
This shall discard the Debug Log regardless of
whether the Latency Monitoring Feature is
Discard Debug  enabled or disabled.
| LMDS-9  | 11  |     | 1   |     |
| ------- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
Log
When set to 02h the debug log will be
discarded so another log can be triggered.
In addition to this none of the other fields of
the Set Features Data structure are valid.
Thus, only the debug log is discarded, and
02h  the Latency Monitor feature is not reset or
loaded with any new values from the Set
Features command.
This shall discard the Debug Log regardless of
whether the Latency Monitoring Feature is
enabled or disabled.

4.15.12  Latency Monitor (Feature Identifier C5h) Get Features
A Get Features command for Feature Identifier C5h should not be issued because no useful information is
returned.  GETF-4 specifies the acceptable values of the NSID field in a Get Features command.
157

Requirement ID  Description
The returned value depends on the contents of the Select (SEL) field in the Get Features
command.
If the Select (SEL) field is cleared to 000b (current value), set to 001b (default value), or set
LMGF-1
to 010b (saved value), then the device shall clear Dword 0 of the completion queue entry to
zero.
If the Select (SEL) field is set to 011b (i.e., Capabilities), see GETF-5.

DSSDPSS-1
NVMe Power State whose Maximum Power (MP) is less than or equal to the number of the
DSSD Power State in watts (see DCLP-9 and DSSDPSD-3).

Features command and the number of that DSSD Power State is less than the Minimum
DSSDPSS-2
DSSD Power State (see DCLP-8), the device shall abort the Set Features command with
Invalid Field in Command status.

4.15.17  Telemetry Profile (Feature Identifier C8h) Set Features
| 4.15.17.1  Telemetry Profiles  |     |     |     |     |
| ------------------------------ | --- | --- | --- | --- |
Telemetry profiles enable the following to be configured:
•  Data Area 1 Last Block
•  Data Area 2 Last Block
•  Statistic Area Location and Size
•  Event FIFO Start and End locations and number of Event FIFOs
In the Telemetry Controller-Initiated log page and Telemetry Host-Initiated log page there is the Number of
Telemetry Profiles Supported field.  This field enables the device to report the number of Telemetry Profiles
supported.  There is also a Telemetry Profile Selected field.  This reports what profile is currently selected.  The
Telemetry Profile Selected field can be changed through Set Features.  The Telemetry Controller-Initiated log
page and Telemetry Host-Initiated log page can then be read to see the format of the Telemetry Profile.  Having
different profiles enables the device to optimize debug for different situations.

4.15.19  DSSD Asynchronous Event Configuration (Feature Identifier C9h) Set Features
This Feature controls the DSSD events that cause an asynchronous event notification to be sent to the host.  If
the condition for an event is true when the corresponding notice indicated in Command Dword 11 is enabled
and there’s an outstanding Asynchronous Event Request command, then that event is sent to the host.  If the
notice indicated in Command Dword 11 is disabled, then that event is not sent to the host.

Requirement ID Dword Field Bits Field Description
If this bit is set to 1b, then:
• the Error Reporting AEN is sent to the host as a
consequence of an error event unless the device
is unable to send that AEN because:
o the device is unable to generate
command completions; or
o there is no outstanding Asynchronous
Event command, and the device is
unable to process commands submitted
to the Admin Queue; and
• the Controller Fatal Status bit in the in-band
Controller Status property shall not be set to 1b
when an error occurs; however, the Controller
Fatal Status bit in the out-of-band Controller
Health Data Structure shall still be set to 1b.
Error Reporting AENs are processed as Notice
(asynchronous) events (see DSSD-AEN-1).
If this bit is cleared to 0b, or the controller is unable to
complete an Error Reporting AEN, then:
• the Error Reporting AEN shall not be sent to the
host; and
• the Controller Fatal Status bit in the in-band
Controller Status property and in the in-band
and out-of-band Controller Health Data
Structure shall be set to 1b when an error event
occurs.
This bit specifies whether an Asynchronous Event
Notification is sent to the host for a DSSD Media Ready
Event. The DSSD Media Ready Event occurs during
device initialization when the device is ready to
successfully respond to Admin commands that access
Enable Media media and IO commands. This event shall occur within
SDAEC-18 11 1
Ready AENs the timespan defined by TTR-2.
If this bit is set to 1b, then the Media Ready AEN is sent
to the host. That Media Ready AEN is processed as a
One-Shot (asynchronous) event (see DSSD-AEN-2).
If this bit is cleared to 0b, then the Media Ready AEN is
not sent to the host.
SDAEC-15 13:12 Reserved All Shall be cleared to zero.
SDAEC-16 14 UUID Index 31:0 Shall be set per UUID-3.

4.15.21  Idle Wake Up Time Configuration (Feature Identifier CAh) Set Features
This Set Features defines the amount of time the device has to wake up to complete a 4 KiB read command from
being in a low power idle mode which is transparent to the host assuming the device is in the L0 state.   If the
Phy is not in the L0 state, the time to transition to L0 is not included in the wake-up time.  This functionality is
independent of the 5 W idle requirement (see PWR-6).
| Requirement ID  | Dword             | Field    | Bits                                         | Field Description  |
| --------------- | ----------------- | -------- | -------------------------------------------- | ------------------ |
|                 |                   | Command  | Shall be set as defined in NVM Express Base  |                    |
| SIDLE-1         | 0                 |          | 31:16                                        |                    |
|                 | Identifier (CID)  |          | Specification.                               |                    |
PRP or SGL for  Shall be cleared to 00b to specify that PRPs are used.
| SIDLE-2  | 0   | Data Transfer  | 15:14  |     |
| -------- | --- | -------------- | ------ | --- |
(PSDT)
| SIDLE-3  | 0   | Reserved   | 13:10  Shall be cleared to zero.  |     |
| -------- | --- | ---------- | --------------------------------- | --- |
|          |     | Fused      | Shall be cleared to 00b.          |     |
| SIDLE-4  | 0   | Operation  | 9:8                               |     |
(FUSE)
| SIDLE-5  | 0  Opcode (OPC)  |             | 7:0  Shall be set to 09h.  |     |
| -------- | ---------------- | ----------- | -------------------------- | --- |
|          |                  | Namespace   | See GETF-4.                |     |
| SIDLE-6  | 1                | Identifier  | 31:0                       |     |
(NSID)
| SIDLE-7  | 3:2  | Reserved  | All  Shall be cleared to zero.  |     |

5 PCIe Requirements
The following are PCIe requirements:
Requirement ID Description
The device shall support a PCIe Maximum Payload Size (MPS) of 512 bytes or larger. When
the device transmits data, the device shall use the largest MPS possible. Changes to the
PCI-1
MPS shall take effect immediately without requiring a Controller Reset or any other type of
reset.
The device shall support modification of PCIe TLP completion timeout range as defined by
PCI-2
the PCI Express Base Specification.
The vendor shall disclose the vendor-specific timeout range definition in the “Completion
PCI-3
Timeout Ranges Supported” field in the PCI Express Base Specification.
PCI-4 The device shall support disabling PCIe Completion Timeout.
The device shall perform a PCIe Fundamental Reset when PERST# is asserted, and main
power has not been removed even if firmware is hung.
PCI-5
The device firmware shall initialize when PERST# is de-asserted, regardless of whether the
device firmware was hung when PERST# was asserted.
PCI-6 PCIe Function Level Reset shall be supported.
PCI-7 Obsolete. See PCI-5.
PCI-8 The device shall not expose a BAR4 or a BAR5 if neither CMB nor PMR is supported.
PCI-9 The device shall support MSI-X.
PCI-10 The MSI-X table shall reside in BAR0.
PCI-11 If implemented, the MSI capability structure in configuration space shall be 4-byte aligned.
Any optional PCI features supported by the device not described in this document shall be
PCI-12
clearly documented and disclosed to the customer.
PCI-13 The device shall support Completion Timeout Ranges A, B and C.
PCI-14 The device shall support Relaxed Ordering.
The device shall not set the Relaxed Ordering bit in transactions it initiates as a Requester
that require strong ordering (i.e., transactions that would violate the NVMe protocol or
result in data corruption if re-ordered shall clear the Relaxed Ordering bit to 0b). For
PCI-15
example, the Enable Relaxed Ordering bit in transactions initiated by the device as a
Requester shall be cleared to 0b in MSI/MSI-X writes, writes to the Completion Queue Entry,
etc.
PCI-16 The device shall set the Relaxed Ordering bit in data DMAs, if Relaxed Ordering is enabled.
The device shall support all link speeds between the lowest link speed and the highest link
PCI-17 speed, inclusive (e.g., a device compliant with the PCI Express Base Specification Revision
6.2 shall support link speeds of 2.5 GT/s, 5.0 GT/s, 8 GT/S, 16 GT/s, 32 GT/s, and 64 GT/s).
172

Requirement ID Description
PCI-18 The device shall not require Device Specific Initialization (DSI).
The device shall not perform a soft reset when transitioning from D3hot to D0 (i.e.,
PCI-19
No_Soft_Reset bit in the Power Management Control/Status Register shall be set to 1b).
PCI-20 The device shall not support BARs that map to I/O Space.
All BARs that map to Memory Space shall be 64-bit capable (i.e., bits 2:1 of the BAR shall be
PCI-21
set to 10b) and shall support the full 64-bit address space.
The sum of the size of all BARs for a single non-SR-IOV function or SR-IOV Physical Function
PCI-22 that maps to Memory Space shall be less than or equal to 1 MiB if neither CMB nor PMR is
supported.
The device shall require a maximum of one PCI bus number (e.g., no PCIe switches are
PCI-23
allowed).
The device’s DMA engines shall support the full 64-bit address space with uniform
PCI-24
performance across the entire address range.
The Device Serial Number Extended Capability shall be supported except for virtual
functions. All functions on all ports of a device that implement this capability shall return
PCI-25 the same serial number value. The serial number shall be unique for each device and
independent from all other unique identifiers on the device (e.g., for namespaces,
controllers, etc.).
PCI-26 The device shall support the Advanced Error Reporting Extended Capability.
The device shall silently discard (following normal data link layer processing) without logging
or signaling an error, any PCIe VDMs targeting a Function while it is in Function Level Reset
(FLR). When an FLR is initiated for a Function, any already-received PCIe VDMs still being
PCI-27
processed by that Function shall be silently discarded.
This requirement prohibits non-silent-discard behavior during an FLR that is allowed by the
PCI Express Base Specification.
PCI-28 The device shall support Address Translation Services (ATS).
While any one or more Functions on the device are in the D3hot power state, MCTP over
PCIe VDM processing shall be fully operational and the device shall not generate errors for
valid MCTP over PCIe VDMs received while in this state. For example, while in this state, the
PCI-29 device shall be able to successfully process MCTP over PCIe VDM requests, transmit the
response, and shall be able to transmit MCTP messages for any asynchronous events that
occur and are enabled.
This requirement applies to all supported MCTP message types (e.g., NVMe-MI, SPDM, etc.).
PCIe non-Fundamental Resets (e.g., Function Level Reset, hot reset, or reset due to a link
down/link disabled condition) shall not clear the device’s captured PCIe bus number(s) or
PCI-30
MCTP Endpoint ID(s). This is required so that devices can continue to communicate via
MCTP over PCIe VDM following these types of resets without having to be re-initialized.
173

Requirement ID Description
PCIe Fundamental Resets shall clear the captured PCIe bus number(s) as required by the PCI
Express Base Specification and shall clear the MCTP Endpoint ID(s) as required by the MCTP
PCIe Transport Binding Specification.
If an MCTP over PCIe VDM would otherwise signal Unsupported Request (e.g., ID Routed
PCI-31 Message targeting a Function that is not implemented) is received, then the device shall
silently discard that message.
In addition to responding to Broadcast from Root Complex as required by the MCTP PCIe
VDM Binding Specification, a PCIe VDM Management Endpoint shall respond to Route by ID
PCI-32 Message Requests for the following MCTP control messages:
• Prepare for Endpoint Discovery; and
• Endpoint Discovery.
PERST# shall not be treated as a power cycle. For example, PERST#:
• shall not cause TCG Opal devices to go to the Read Locked/Write Locked state (i.e.,
PERST# maps to the TCG reset type of Hardware Reset, not a Power Cycle, as
defined by the TCG Storage Interface Interactions Specification) if the host has not
PCI-33
configured a TCG HW Reset as one of the Reset Types that can lock the device’s
locking ranges on LockOnReset in addition to Power Cycle; and
• shall not cause commands prohibited via the NVMe Lockdown command to be un-
prohibited.
PERST# shall not cause RW1CS bits defined by the PCI Express Base Specification (e.g., bits
PCI-34
in the Uncorrectable Error Status and Correctable Error Status registers) to be cleared.
PCI-35 The device shall not support either the D1 or the D2 power management states.
If any power-of-two-sized access, up to 8-bytes in size, to the memory pointed to by any of
the NVMe device's BARs (e.g., access to controller registers) is aligned to a power-of-two
boundary equal to the size of the access (e.g., a 2-byte access aligned to a 2-byte boundary,
a 4-byte access aligned to a 4-byte boundary, etc.), then the access shall not be considered a
restricted programming model violation (i.e., the access shall be processed successfully
unless some other error unrelated to a restricted programming model violation is
encountered).
PCI-36 Support is optional for any accesses greater than 8-bytes in size to the memory pointed to
by NVMe BAR0/BAR1 (e.g., access to controller registers). The restricted programming
model for the memory pointed to by BARs other than BAR0/BAR1 may support additional
access sizes as required by the device vendor.
For any access that results in a restricted programming model violation, the request shall be
handled as an Unsupported Request or Completer Abort as permitted for restricted
programming model violations as defined by the PCI Express Base Specification (e.g., the
device firmware shall not hang due to a restricted programming model violation).
If the device receives an MCTP over PCIe VDM that is invalid due to an MCTP base layer
error or MCTP message-type layer (e.g., NVMe-MI, SPDM) error, then the error shall be
PCI-37
reported, if possible, at the MCTP base layer or MCTP message-type layer respectively;
otherwise, the invalid MCTP over PCIe VDM shall be silently discarded.
174

Requirement ID Description
This requirement applies to all supported MCTP message types (e.g., NVMe-MI, SPDM, etc.).
A Function Level Reset to a Function other than the Function associated with the MCTP
PCI-38 endpoint shall have no impact on MCTP traffic on the Function associated with the MCTP
endpoint.
The device shall perform a PCIe Conventional Reset per the PCI Express Base Specification
(e.g., resetting PCIe-defined state machines, setting PCIe-defined registers to default, etc.)
when main power has not been removed and any of the following conditions occur, even if
PCI-39
the firmware is not functioning (e.g., has asserted or is otherwise non-responsive):
• the PCIe link is disabled; or
• the device is reset by a PCIe hot reset.
The device shall comply with PCI-SIG requirements for supported TLP sizes, including
PCI-40 support for TLP writes to PRP memory addresses with 64-byte alignment and 64-byte
granularity.
MCTP over PCIe VDM shall be supported by PCIe Function 0 on each port and shall not be
PCI-41
supported by any other PCIe Function.
PCI-42 For PCIe Gen6 devices, L0p shall be supported.
5.1 Boot Requirements
Requirement ID Description
The device shall support the UEFI 2.0 and all later versions of the Tianocore EDKII NVMe
BOOT-1
driver.
BOOT-2 The device shall neither support nor include an option ROM.

04h) in PCI Express Base Specification.

PCIERR-5 Unexpected Completion Status (UCS)
The host is able to read and clear the
PCIERR-6 Completer Abort Status (CAS) contents of this register as appropriate.

in PCI Express Base Specification.

5.3 Low Power Modes
Requirement ID Description
ASPM shall be disabled after a power cycle or PCIe resets as defined by the PCI Express Base
LPWR-1
Specification.
LPWR-2 The device shall support the PCIe ASPM L1 power state.
5.4 PCIe Eye Capture
Requirement ID Description
A utility shall be provided that takes the entire Physical Interface Receiver Eye Opening
EYE-1 Measurement log page as an input and decodes the Eye Data field of each lane in the log
page.
6 Optional Device Features
Features in this section are optional. If the feature is implemented, it shall follow the requirements in this
section.
6.1 Flexible Data Placement Requirements
If Flexible Data Placement is supported, then the Generic Flexible Data Placement Requirements and a minimum
of one of the Flexible Data Placement configurations shall be supported:
6.1.1 Generic Flexible Data Placement Requirements
Requirement ID Description
FDPG-1 Obsolete (see NVMe-OPT-16).
176

Requirement ID Description
It shall be clearly disclosed to the customer which FDP Event Types are supported and what
FDPG-2 additional fields related to this are supported with each event type (FDP Event Flags, PID,
NSID, Reclaim Group Identifier, Reclaim Unit Handle Identifier, etc.)
6.1.2 FDP Single Reclaim Group Configuration 1
Requirement ID Description
FDPSRG-1 The number of advertised reclaim groups (NRG) shall be 1.
FDPSRG-2 The device shall support a minimum of 8 reclaim unit handles.
FDPSRG-3 The device shall set Volatile Write Cache Present to 0b (not supported).
The device shall support an FDP configuration with a minimum of 8 reclaim unit handles of
FDPSRG-4
Reclaim Unit Handle Type Initially Isolated.
FDPSRG-5 Obsolete. Moved to FDPSRG2-2.
FDPSRG-6 Single reclaim group configurations shall support a minimum of 8 namespaces.
Single reclaim group configurations shall support SECTOR-4 and DIX-1 in an FDP
FDPSRG-7
configuration.
6.1.3 FDP Single Reclaim Group Configuration 2
Requirement ID Description
The device shall support all the requirements in FDP Single Reclaim Group Configuration 1
FDPSRG2-1
section 6.1.2 except FDPSRG-4.
The device shall support an FDP configuration with a minimum of 8 reclaim unit handles of
FDPSRG2-2
Reclaim Unit Handle Type Persistently Isolated.
6.1.4 FDP Die Placement Configuration
Requirement ID Description
The number of advertised reclaim groups (NRG) shall match the number of flash dies in the
FDPDP-1
NVM subsystem.
The configuration shall support a minimum of 8 reclaim unit handles. In other words, it
FDPDP-2
shall be possible to utilize (NRG) x 8 placement identifiers simultaneously.

7 Reliability
7.1 Uncorrectable Bit Error Rate
Requirement ID Description
The device shall support an Uncorrectable Bit Error Rate (UBER) of < 1 sector per 1018 bits
UBER-1 read. Physical device testing is only required to demonstrate an Uncorrectable Bit Error
Rate (UBER) of < 1 sector per 1017 bits read (as per JESD218B method).
7.2 Power On/Off Requirements
7.2.1 Time to Ready and Shutdown Requirements
Requirement ID Description
The device shall be able to process the Identify command with a successful completion
TTR-1 within 1 second of CC.EN being set to 1b provided a Shutdown is not in progress when
CC.EN is set to 1b. Some models may allow a longer time (see Section 13 Device Profiles).
The device shall be able to process I/O and Admin commands that require access to media
with a successful completion within 20 seconds after CC.EN has been set to 1b. Some
TTR-2
models require a different time (see Section 13 Device Profiles). See TTR-22 for additional
requirements for time to ready after PCIe Conventional Reset.
The device shall be able to process Admin commands with a successful completion as soon
TTR-3 as CSTS.RDY = 1. Slower processing of Admin commands that require media access is
acceptable while the media is becoming ready.
The device shall keep CSTS.RDY = 0 until the device is able to process Admin commands.
TTR-4 Some models may have additional requirements before CSTS.RDY can be set to 1 (see
Section 13 Device Profiles).
The Shutdown Notification completion (i.e., the CSTS.SHST set to 10b) shall be received
TTR-5
within 10 seconds after the start of a normal shutdown (i.e., after CC.SHN is set to 01b).
TTR-6 The device shall support both the CC.SHN Normal and Abrupt Shutdown Notifications.
After a normal shutdown is completed successfully, the device shall not enter a
TTR-7
rebuild/recovery mode on the next power on.
A normal shutdown shall trigger flushing to non-volatile memory of any content within the
TTR-8 device’s internal cache(s) (e.g., SRAM/DRAM), if present, which is required to be non-
volatile.
TTR-9 Obsolete. See NVMe-CFG-3.
TTR-10 Obsolete. Moved to PLP-1.
179

Requirement ID Description
TTR-11 Obsolete. Moved to PLP-2.
Metadata rebuild due to any reason (e.g., unexpected power loss) shall not exceed 120
TTR-12
seconds and the device shall meet its latency requirements after this.
TTR-13 Obsolete. Moved to PLP-3.
TTR-14 Obsolete. Moved to PLP-4.
In case of a successful Normal shutdown operation (CC.SHN = 1 set by the NVMe device
TTR-15
driver), no data loss is tolerated even if PLP has failed.
TTR-16 Any shutdown event shall not make the device non-functional under any conditions.
TTR-17 Obsolete. Moved to PLP-5.
TTR-18 Obsolete. Moved to PLP-6.
When the CC.SHN register is written to notify the device to shut down it shall not be
TTR-19 assumed that power will be lost even after CC.EN is cleared to 0. Under these conditions
the device shall continue to function properly based on the NVMe and PCIe Specifications.
The device shall be able to successfully respond to Configuration space accesses within 1s
TTR-20
from de-assertion of PERST#.
TTR-21 Obsolete, see GDAEC-2 and GDAEC-3.
Upon completion of a PCIe Conventional Reset, the device shall start initializing the media
and within 20 seconds from the completion of the PCIe Conventional Reset shall be able to
successfully process:
in-band I/O and Admin commands requiring media access, assuming CC.EN has been set to
1b; and
out-of-band Admin commands requiring media access, including prior to the in-band host
TTR-22 enabling the controller.
Some models require a different time (see Section 13 Device Profiles)
If a PCIe Conventional Reset occurs while a device is shutdown (i.e., the CSTS.SHST field is
set to 10b), then this requirement may cause the device to transition to a state where a
power loss would be unexpected. This requirement overrides the requirement in the NVM
Express Base specification for the controller to be ready to be powered off until CC.EN
transitions from 0b to 1b following a controller shutdown.
TTR-23 The device shall not support NVM Subsystem Shutdown.
7.2.2 Incomplete/Unsuccessful Shutdown
An incomplete/unsuccessful shutdown is a Normal or Abrupt power down that did not complete 100% of the
shutdown sequence for any reason that causes the device to be unable to guarantee data/metadata integrity
(e.g., firmware hang/crash, capacitor failure, PLP circuit failure, etc.).
Requirement ID Description
When the power-loss protection mechanism fails for any reason while power is applied, the
INCS-1
device shall:
180

Requirement ID Description
• set Critical Warning bit 4 to 1b in the SMART / Health Information log page (Log
Identifier 02h);
• send an NVM subsystem Reliability SMART / Health Status AEN, if that AEN is
enabled; and
• transition to the write behavior as defined in the PLP Failure Mode (see Section
4.15.5 PLP Failure Mode (Feature Identifier C2h Set Features).
The device shall incorporate a shutdown checksum or flag as the very last piece of data
INCS-2
written to flash to detect incomplete shutdown.
The checksum or flag in INCS-2 shall be used on power-up to confirm that the previous
INCS-3
shutdown was 100% successful.
An incomplete/unsuccessful shutdown that causes the device to be unable to guarantee
data/metadata integrity shall result in an increase in the Incomplete Shutdowns field
INCS-4 (SMART-15) in the SMART / Health Information Extended log page (Log Identifier C0h). on
the subsequent power up, the device shall set bit 3 of the Critical Warning field in the
SMART / Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h) to 1b.
If the device is in read-only mode (i.e., bit 3 in the Critical Warning field is set to 1b in the
SMART / Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h)) for any reason, then the device
INCS-5
shall still support NVMe Admin commands, including commands that result in a purge (see
SEC-43).
If the Error Recovery log page (Log Identifier C1h) is supported, when the device increments
the Incomplete Shutdowns field in SMART / Health Information Extended log page (Log
Identifier C0h), it shall use the following recovery procedure at the next power up:
INCS-6
If the Error Recovery log page (Log Identifier C1h) is not supported, when the device
INCS-7 increments the Incomplete Shutdowns field in SMART / Health Information Extended log
page (Log Identifier C0h), it shall use the following recovery procedure at the next power up:
181

Requirement ID Description
7.3 End to End Internal Data Protection
Requirement ID Description
All user data and metadata shall be protected using overlapping protection mechanisms
E2E-1 throughout the entire read and write path in the device including all storage elements
(registers, caches, SRAM, DRAM, NAND, etc.).
At least one bit of correction and 2 bits of detection is required for all memories. This shall
E2E-2
be for all memories regardless of function.
The entire DRAM addressable space shall be protected with at least one-bit correction and 2
bits of detection scheme (SECDED). This includes but is not limited to the following:
• Flash translation layer (FTL).
• Mapping tables (including metadata related to deallocated LBAs).
E2E-3
• Journal entries.
• Firmware scratch pad.
• System variables.
• Firmware code.
E2E-4 Silent data corruption shall not be tolerated under any circumstances.
The device shall include a mechanism to protect against returning the data from the wrong
logical block address (LBA), including previous copies from the same LBA, to the host. It is
E2E-5 acceptable if the device stores additional/modified information to provide protection
against returning wrong data to the host. Device shall perform host LBA integrity checking
on all transfers to and from the media.
All device metadata, firmware, firmware variables, and other device system data shall be
E2E-6
protected by at least a single bit detection scheme.
Any memory buffers that are utilized to accelerate data transfer (read-ahead buffers for
E2E-7
example) shall follow the protection scheme outlined in E2E-5.
182

7.4 Behavior on Firmware Crash, Panic or Assert
Requirement ID Description
While the device is in a failed state in which it can no longer accept Write commands (e.g.,
CRASH-1 firmware crash, error, or assert), the device shall allow read access only if it can guarantee
data integrity.
While the device is in a failed state, that is not a controller failure (e.g., firmware crash, HW
error, or assert), the device shall still support NVMe Admin commands including the ability
CRASH-2 to read any failure logs from the device to determine the nature of the failure.
After a controller failure, the device may fail Admin commands sent by the host prior to
completion of the Error Reset Action in the Error Recovery workflow (see EREC-2).
Upon device completion of the actions specified in Error Reset Action (see EREC-2) and
Device Recovery Action (see EREC-3), if the device is successfully recovered from a failed
CRASH-3
state, then the device shall function normally as specified in this specification including read
and write access at full performance.
CRASH-4 Obsolete.
The device shall have a mechanism (e.g., watchdog timer) to allow recovery from hangs of
CRASH-5 the firmware and hardware. The timeout interval of this mechanism shall be less than 2
seconds.

The device shall meet an MTBF of 2.5 million hours (AFR of <= 0.35% per JEDEC JESD 218)
under the following environmental conditions:

The device shall meet an MTBF of 2.0 million hours (AFR of <= 0.44% per JEDEC JESD 218)
REL-2

(WCTEMP) with less than 1% of the device power on time above WCTEMP.
The device shall have no exposed raw copper on any component. All copper surfaces, pads,

7.6 Background Data Refresh
Requirement ID Description
The device shall support background data refresh while the device is powered on to ensure
BKGND-1
there is no data-loss due to power-on retention issues.
The device shall be designed and tested to support the normal NAND operating
BKGND-2
temperature.
Background data refresh shall cover the entire device and be designed to continuously run
BKGND-3
in the background and not just during idle periods.
7.7 Wear-leveling
Requirement ID Description
The device shall utilize the entire Endurance Group media capacity range whenever the
device needs to wear-level a block. The device shall not restrict the wear-leveling range to a
WRL-1
subset of the Endurance Group media capacity unless otherwise specified. If the device
does not support Endurance Groups, it shall wear-level across the entire physical media.
184

7.8 Power Loss Protection
Requirement ID Description
PLP-1 The device shall support full power-loss protection for all acknowledged data and metadata.
PLP-2 The Power-loss protection health check shall not impact I/O latency and performance.
Power-loss protection health check shall be performed by the device at power-on (prior to
PLP-3
accepting any writes) and at least once every time interval as specified in SPLPI-13.
While performing the power-loss protection health check, the device shall still have enough
PLP-4
energy to be able to handle an abrupt power loss properly.
The firmware/hardware algorithm shall deploy safeguards to prevent false detection of
power loss protection failure. Example of a false detection would be a glitch in any of the
PLP-5
power loss circuitry readings which would cause a transient event to trigger a false power
loss protection failure when the power loss protection hardware is healthy.
The device shall implement a power-loss protection (PLP) health check which can detect the
capacitor holdup energy margin reported in the Capacitor Health field specified in SMART-
PLP-6 19 in SMART / Heath Information Extended log page (Log Identifier C0h). The PLP health
check shall not just check for open/short capacitor conditions but shall measure the true
available margin energy.
PLP-7 The factory default PLP Health Check Interval shall be 15 minutes (see GPLPI-2).
The default PLP Health Check Interval of 15 minutes (see GPLPI-2) shall not cause the device
PLP-8
to violate REL-1 or REL-2.
The device shall use the following workflow for the PLP Health Check (see INCS-1) for PLP
PLP-9
Loss details):

7.9 Device Limits
Requirement ID Description
The device shall not have any architectural restrictions, other than P/E cycle restrictions of
the NAND, on the number of times any of the following events can occur:
• Firmware downloads and activation supported (see FWUP-2); or
• Changing password when taking/changing ownership via TCG; or
DEVLMT-1 • Commands that result in a purge (see SEC-43); or
• Power cycles; or
• Set Features command/Get Features command (including power state changes); or
• Log page or debug log retrievals.
This is not meant to be a test until fail requirement.
8 Endurance
8.1 Endurance Data
Requirement ID Description
The device documentation shall include the number of physical bytes able to be written to
ENDUD-1
the device assuming a write amplification of 1. The units should be gigabytes (10^9 bytes).
The preconditioning steps to test device performance at end-of-life are:
• 50/50 Read/Write workload (by number of I/Os).
• 4 KiB Read accesses aligned to 4 KiB boundaries.
• 128 KiB Write accesses aligned to 128 KiB boundaries.
• Random pattern of Read addresses.
ENDUD-2 • Sequential pattern of Write addresses.
• 100% active range.
• 80% full device (80% data, 20% free space).
• 0% compressible data.
• Ambient temperature 35°C (95°F).
• Short-stroked device if capacity is 2 TB or greater (see EOL-2).
The Percentage Used in the SMART / Heath Information log page (Log Identifier 02h) shall
ENDUD-3 track linearly with bytes written and at 100% it shall match the EOL value specified in
ENDUD-1.
8.2 Retention Conditions
Since there are several factors that impact the device endurance, the following table provides the requirements
for the datacenter environment:
187

Requirement ID Description
Non-Operational (Powered-off) device data retention time (end of life) shall be at least 1
RETC-1 month at 40°C (104°F). See Section 13 Device Profiles for specific retention requirements.
Specific Devices Profiles may have longer data retention time requirements.
Operating (Powered-on) data retention shall be at least 7 years. For purposes of this
requirement, the assumption is that the Terabytes Written (TBW) capability of the devices is
RETC-2
used linearly over the lifetime. This requirement does not imply any specific warranty
period.
The device shall not throttle its performance based on the endurance metric (endurance
RETC-3
throttling).
8.3 Shelf Life
Requirement ID Description
A new device may be kept as a datacenter spare and therefore shall be fully functional even
SLIFE-1 if it sits on the shelf for at least 5 years at 25°C (77°F) before getting installed in the server.
The device shall be new in box factory state.
SLIFE-2 Shelf-life shall be documented and provided to the customer.
8.4 End-of-Life (EOL)
Requirement ID Description
Several types of samples are required for EOL testing:
a. Beginning of Life (Short stroked if required by EOL-2).
b. End of Life (Short stroked if required by EOL-2).
EOL-1 c. End of Life (Not short stroked if different than item b).
EOL is defined as the Total Bytes Written (TBW) specification has been surpassed (see
ENDUD-1) or the non-volatile media endurance limit (e.g., NAND cycling limit causes the
block to be unwritable) has been reached; whichever is earliest.
On 2 TB or larger devices, there shall be a method to “short stroke” the device. Media
reserved for background operations shall be proportionally adjusted. Short Stroke firmware
EOL-2
capacity shall be reduced to a range of 10% to 3% of full capacity. Short stroke shall cover
all the channels/dies/planes while maintaining the native performance of the device.
EOL-3 Obsolete.
The device shall continue to operate in a read/write mode until the conditions in EOL-5 are
EOL-4 reached or until another type of error causes the device to be unable to continue to operate
in read/write mode (e.g., the device enter read-only mode due to the conditions in INCS-4).
The device shall switch to Read Only Mode (ROM) when the Available Spare field in the
SMART / Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h) reaches 0%. A value of 0%
EOL-5
represents the device state where there is an insufficient number of spare blocks to support
Host writes. The Available Spare field shall report a value of 0% before the device exhausts
188

Requirement ID Description
all available spare blocks so that there are still sufficient available spare blocks remaining to
handle blocks going bad during read operations.
When the device switches to ROM due to this condition, bit 2 and bit 3 of the Critical
Warning field in the SMART / Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h) shall be set to
1b.
If the value reported in the Available Spares field falls below the value reported in the
Available Spare Threshold field, then the device shall set bit 0 of the Critical Warning field in
the SMART / Health Information log page to 1b and generate a SMART / Health Status event
if that event is enabled and an Asynchronous Event Request command is outstanding.
The device shall have enough spare blocks so that the Percentage Used field value in the
SMART / Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h) reaches 100% prior to the
EOL-6
Available Spare field value falling below the Available Spare Threshold field value. See
ENDUD-1 and ENDUD-3 for related Percentage Used field value requirements.
The update granularity for the Percentage Used field and Available Spare field in the SMART
EOL-7
/ Health Information log page (Log Identifier 02h) shall be 1%.
The Available Spare Threshold shall be set such that the Available Spare does not reach 0%
EOL-8 for at least three days after crossing the Available Spare Threshold assuming a worst-case
write workload.
9 Thermal
9.1 Data Center Altitude
Requirement ID Description
Support for devices in data centers located at an altitude of up to 10,000 feet above sea
level is required (e.g., thermals, cosmic rays, etc.). When considering thermals, there shall
THERM-1
be no de-rating up to 6,000 feet above sea level. Above 6,000 feet the derating shall be
0.9°C (1.6°F)/1000ft.
A thermal study with each platform is required and shall be provided to the customer. The
THERM-2 thermal design shall be validated up to 35°C (95°F) ambient temperature for the platform
with a worst-case airflow of 1.5 meters per second at sea level.
THERM-3 The device shall operate normally with relative humidity to be between 10% and 90%.
9.2 Thermal Throttling
Requirement ID Description
The device shall implement a thermal throttling mechanism to protect the device in case of
TTHROTTLE-1 a failure or an excursion that causes the device’s temperature to increase above its
maximum specified temperature. This mechanism shall check device temperature at a
189

Requirement ID Description
frequency sufficient to ensure that the thermal throttling mechanism protects the device.
This temperature check frequency shall be at least once per second.
When the device begins throttling performance due to an over temperature condition, an
Asynchronous Event Request shall be completed with the Asynchronous Event Type field set
to 001b (SMART / Health status) and the Asynchronous Event Information field set to 01h
TTHROTTLE-2
(Temperature Threshold), if that event is enabled and an Asynchronous Event Request
command is outstanding. The device shall set bit 1 of the SMART / Health Information log
page (Log Identifier 02h) Critical Warning field to 1b.
Thermal throttling shall only be engaged under conditions that are able to cause significant
reduction in device service life, such as excessive server ambient temperature. The required
behavior is illustrated in the following figure:
TTHROTTLE-3
The firmware algorithm shall deploy safeguards to prevent a false activation of either
thermal throttling or thermal shutdown. An example of a false activation would be a glitch
TTHROTTLE-4
in any of the sensor readings which would cause the composite temperature to reach the
thermal throttling or thermal shutdown limit.
A composite temperature of 77°C (170.6°F) shall be used to start throttling. Single stage and
TTHROTTLE-5
multi-stage throttling are both allowed.
TTHROTTLE-6 Thermal throttling shall not start based on the rate of temperature increase or slew rate.
When the device is in the thermal throttling state and the temperature drops back down
below 75°C (167°F), the device shall exit the thermal throttling state and an Asynchronous
Event Request shall be completed with the Asynchronous Event Type field set to 001b
TTHROTTLE-7 (SMART / Health status) and the Asynchronous Event Information field set to 01h
(Temperature Threshold), if that event is enabled and an Asynchronous Event Request
command is outstanding. The device shall clear bit 1 of the SMART / Health Information log
page (Log Identifier 02h) Critical Warning field to 0b.
When the device reaches a critical temperature on any component it shall report a
composite temperature of 85°C (185°F) and an Asynchronous Event Request shall be
TTHROTTLE-8
completed with the Asynchronous Event Type field set to 001b (SMART / Health status) and
the Asynchronous Event Information field set to 01h (Temperature Threshold), if that event
190

Requirement ID Description
is enabled and an Asynchronous Event Request command is outstanding, before the device
shuts off to protect itself.
The device shall report a value of 015Eh (77°C) (170.6°F) in the Warning Composite
TTHROTTLE-9
Temperature Threshold (WCTEMP) field of the Identify Controller Data structure.
The device shall report a value of 0166h (85°C) (185°F) in the Critical Composite
TTHROTTLE-10
Temperature Threshold (CCTEMP) field of the Identify Controller Data structure.
If the Composite Temperature is greater than or equal to 77°C (170.6°F), the device shall
update the Warning Composite Temperature Time field of the SMART / Health Information
log page (Log Identifier 02h) once per minute until one of the following occurs:
TTHROTTLE-11
• The device Composite Temperature falls below 75°C (167°F); or
• The device shuts down due to an over Critical Temperature condition; or
• The device is power cycled.
The temperature limits of internal components within the device shall govern the thermal
TTHROTTLE-12 throttling algorithms. In addition, the thermal throttling algorithms shall prevent excessive
case temperature (see TTHROTTLE-14).
In all throttling states including the lowest throttle state, the device shall not enter a read-
only mode and shall continue to attempt to process all commands, including commands
TTHROTTLE-13
that write media, unless the device shuts down, e.g., due to a Critical Temperature
condition.
The critical device case (i.e., touch) temperature shall be the TS2 limits as specified in IEC
62368-1 3rd Edition or later. For non-case devices the hottest surface shall be used for the
TTHROTTLE-14 device touch temperature.
The TS2 100oC limit is prohibited for some form factors (see FFM2-15, FFE1S-13, and FFE1L-
13).
9.3 Temperature Reporting
Requirement ID Description
TRPT-1 The device shall expose the current raw sensor readings from all the sensors on the device.
A device shall report a composite temperature that has an accuracy better than or equal to
+/-1°C (1.8°F) degrees. As a consequence, two devices of the same model shall not report a
TRPT-2
composite temperature greater than 2°C (3.6°F) apart under the same environmental
conditions, slot location, and workload.
A device shall use temperature sensors that have an accuracy better than or equal to +/-1°C
TRPT-3
(1.8°F) degrees.
The vendor shall provide the customer the equation, settings, and thresholds used to
TRPT-4
calculate the composite temperature.
When calculating the composite temperature, the device shall take into account the
TRPT-5
temperature of all of the major thermal components (SOC, DRAM, NAND, PMIC, etc.).
191

Requirement ID Description
The reported composite temperature shall be the same for all controllers in the NVM
TRPT-6
subsystem.
9.4 Thermal Shutdown
Requirement ID Description
The device shall shut down to protect itself against data loss or damage due to extreme
THRMS-1 temperatures. The shutdown temperature value shall be at a composite temperature of
85°C (185°F). Shutdown shall preserve all user data.
The device shall not process NVM I/O commands while in thermal shutdown. If it is safe to
THRMS-2 do so, the device shall process Admin commands (in-band and out-of-band), NVMe-MI
Command Set commands, and PCIe Command Set commands while in thermal shutdown.
The device shall only come out of thermal shutdown as a result of a main power cycle or
THRMS-3
PWRDIS cycling internal device power.
10 Form Factor Requirements
10.1 General Form Factor Requirements
Requirement ID Description
The device shall be compliant to PCI Express Base Specification, Revision 5.0, Version 1.0 (or
GFF-1
later).
GFF-2 The vendor shall provide a PCIe compliance report that demonstrates compliance.
The device shall support lane reversal with all lanes connected or partially connected lanes
on both the lower-numbered lanes and higher-numbered lanes of the device (e.g., a x4
GFF-3
device shall support lane reversal for x4, x2, and x1 connections on both the lower-
numbered lanes and higher-numbered lanes of the device).
The device shall train to x1 when the upstream device provides only one lane, to x2 when 2
GFF-4 lanes are provided and to x4 when 4 lanes are provided. This requirement applies to both
the lower-numbered lanes and higher-numbered lanes of the device.
GFF-5 The device shall support hot swap on form factors that support hot swap.
GFF-6 A CAD file of each supported form factor shall be provided to the customer.
For the purpose of determining when to blink the LED, host-requested activity consists of
processing one or more of the following:
• any I/O command;
GFF-7 • any Admin command whose processing is expected to take more than one second;
or
• any background activity that was initiated by an Admin command if that background
processing is expected to take more than one second.
192

Requirement ID Description
The LED effects of Admin command processing are independent of whether an Admin
command was submitted in-band or out-of-band.
For the purpose of determining when to blink the LED, the following activities are not host-
requested activity:
• internally initiated background activity;
• maintenance activity that is not requested by the host;
GFF-8
• NVMe Basic Management command activity (see Section 11.1 NVMe Basic
Management Command (Appendix A) Requirements); and
• NVMe-MI activity (see Section 11.3 NVMe-MI Requirements) with the exception of
NVMe Admin commands submitted via NVMe-MI.
10.2 Power Consumption Measurement Methodology
Requirement ID Description
The device Max Average Power (MAP) consumption for any workload shall not exceed the
Maximum Power (MP) of the current NVMe Power State measured over a 1 second window
PCM-1 with a sampling rate of 2 ms or less. The measurement duration shall be at least 15 minutes
on a pre-conditioned device. This requirement defines the measurement methodology for
Maximum Sustained Device Power as defined in SFF-TA-1009 revision 3.0.
The device peak power for any workload shall be measured over a 100 uS window with a
PCM-2 sampling interval of 4 uS or less. The measurement duration shall be at least 15 minutes on
a pre-conditioned device.
For devices whose max average power consumption is less than or equal to 25 W, the peak
power shall be no more than 1.5x the max average power. For devices whose max average
power consumption is greater than 25 W but less than or equal to 29W the peak power
PCM-3
shall be no more than 37.5 W. For devices whose max average power consumption is
greater than 29 W, the peak power shall be no more than 1.3x the max average power. The
max average power is defined in PCM-1.
The Maximum Power field in each NVMe Power State Descriptor data structure in the
Identify Controller data structure shall indicate (for the described power state) the
PCM-4
maximum allowed value of the device Max Average Power (MAP) where MAP is measured
as specified by PCM-1.
10.3 Power Levels
Requirement ID Description
The Power Management (Feature Identifier 02h) shall be supported and the NVMe Power
PWR-1 State Descriptor table in Identify Controller Data Structure bytes 3071:2048 shall be filled
out per the NVM Express Base Specification.
PWR-2 Obsolete. See DCLP-9 and Section 4.8.11.1 DSSD Power State Descriptor.
193

Requirement ID Description
The method of measurement for Maximum Average Power (MAP) is defined in PCM-1.
PWR-3 MAP values are reported in the Maximum Power (MP) field of NVMe Power State
Descriptors.
Power state entries above the maximum rated power envelope of the device shall not be
PWR-4 populated in the NVMe Power State Descriptor table in Identify Controller Data Structure
bytes 3071:2048.
The Set Features for Power Management (Feature Identifier 02h) with the SV bit 31 in
PWR-5 Command Dword 10 shall be supported so that the power level can be set and will be saved
across power cycles.
The device, regardless of form factor or capacity, shall have an idle power of 5 W or less per
European Lot 9 regulation without use of the Idle Wake Up Time Configuration Feature (see
PWR-6 Section 4.15.21 Idle Wake Up Time Configuration (Feature Identifier CAh) Set Features).
Devices shall automatically reduce power consumption to 5 W or less when idle without
impacting latency or performance.
The device shall not consume more power than the PCI-SIG Slot Capabilities register Slot
PWR-7
Power Limit regardless of other settings (e.g., DSSD Power State, NVMe Power State).
The device shall not use the same Maximum Power (MP) value in more than one supported
PWR-8
NVMe Power State Descriptor unless otherwise specified.
The device shall not support Non-Operational Power State Permissive Mode (i.e., bit 1 of
PWR-9 the Controller Attributes field in the Identify Controller data structure shall be cleared to
0b).
10.4 M.2 Form Factor Requirements
Requirement ID Description
The device shall adhere to the M.2 specification with a size of 22 mm x 110 mm or 22 mm x
FFM2-1
80 mm.
FFM2-2 The bottom-side height shall not exceed 1.5 mm.
The top-side height shall not exceed 3.2 mm. Some models may need to be thinner (see
FFM2-3
Section 13 Device Profiles).
FFM2-4 The device shall use an M key.
FFM2-5 The device shall support a minimum of PCIe Gen4 x4.
FFM2-6 The device shall support driving an activity LED through the connector via LED_1#.
The LED should be lit solidly while power is applied, and the device is not performing host-
FFM2-7 requested activity (see GFF-8). The LED should blink while the device is performing host-
requested activity (see GFF-7).
The device shall not use any pins that are defined in the M.2 specification for vendor unique
FFM2-8
functionality.

Requirement ID Description
The device shall support a protection scheme that protects against NAND block level
FFM2-9
failures.
The protection scheme must also support NAND plane level failures without data or
FFM2-10
metadata loss.
FFM2-11 The Label shall be placed on the top side of the device.
The device’s SMBus electricals shall comply with version 3.2 (see
FFM2-12 http://www.smbus.org/specs/SMBus_3_2_20220112.pdf) and in PCI Express M.2 Revision
4.2 or later.
The device’s SMBus protocol shall comply with version 3.2 (see
FFM2-13
http://www.smbus.org/specs/SMBus_3_2_20220112.pdf).
The default max average power for M.2 devices shall not exceed 8.25 W and the peak
FFM2-14
power shall comply to PCM-3.
The case (i.e., touch) temperature shall not exceed 80oC (176oF). The 100oC (212oF) TS2
FFM2-15
limit does not apply (see TTHROTTLE-14).

10.7 E3 Form Factor Requirements
Requirement ID Description

requirements of the PCI Express Base Specification.

FFE3-3 the full jitter specified by the PCI Express Base Specification (see FFE3-4).

on assertion/de-assertion of PERST# with or without a power cycle as described in
SFF-TA-1009 and shall not switch clocking modes under any other conditions.

FFE3-4
later).

Revision 6.2 (or later)
10.8 SFF-8639 (U.2/U.3) Form Factor Requirements
Requirement ID Description
The device shall adhere to SFF-TA-1001 revision 1.1 or later and the PCI Express SFF-8639
FF8639-1
Module Specification, Revision 4.0, Version 1.0 (or later).
The device shall support Separate Reference Clocks with Independent SSC (SRIS)
requirements of the PCI Express Base Specification.
Devices shall support SRIS detection and switching as described in the PCI Express SFF-8639
Module Specification (see FF8639-1) and support the full jitter specified by the PCI Express
FF8639-2 Base Specification Revision 4.0.
The device shall support switching between SRIS and common clock on a power cycle and
on assertion/de-assertion of PERST# with or without a power cycle and shall not switch
clocking modes under any other conditions.
197

Requirement ID Description
All 2.5” SFF NVMe devices shall support the activity LED function on Pin 11 of the SFF-8639
connector.
Pin 11 shall assert/de-assert (see FF8639-4) while the device is performing host-requested
activity (see GFF-7). Once asserted due to command processing, pin 11 shall remain
FF8639-3 asserted for 50 ms and then shall be de-asserted for 50 ms. This assert/de-assert behavior
shall continue while command processing continues (i.e., the LED is usually off, but flashes
on and off while commands are processed).
Once pin 11 is de-asserted for 50 ms, it shall remain de-asserted as long as there is no
command processing activity.
Active State (pin asserted and LED on) is defined as logic “0” (i.e., < 0.3 V) on Pin 11.
Inactive State is defined as logic “1” (i.e., > 3.3 V) on Pin 11.
FF8639-4 Device activity other than host-requested activity (e.g., internally initiated background
activity or maintenance routine that is not commanded to be performed from the host)
shall not cause the LED to be in the Active State (logic “0” level). See GFF-8.
