11 Management Support
11.1 NVMe Basic Management Command (Appendix A) Requirements
Requirement ID Description
If the device supports the NVMe Basic Management Command (see DP-CFG-4), then the
device shall support that command as defined in Appendix A of the NVM Express
SMBUS-1 Management Interface Specification, Revision 2.0: ( https://nvmexpress.org/wp-
content/uploads/NVM-Express-Management-Interface-Specification-Revision-2.0-
2024.08.05-Ratified.pdf ).
SMBus Block Read protocol and Byte Read protocol shall be supported. As an override of
SMBUS-2 the NVM Express Management Interface Specification, SMBus Block Write protocol and Byte
Write protocol shall also be supported.
The device shall implement the SMBus format as show in Section 11.2 - NVMe Basic
SMBUS-3
Management Command (Appendix A) Data Format.
Unless otherwise noted, the default value for the Firmware Update Flags field (byte 91) in
SMBUS-4
the SMBus Data structure shall be set to FFh.
The Secure Boot Failure Feature Reporting Supported bit at offset 243 shall be supported
SMBUS-5
and set to 1b.
When there is a secure boot failure the device shall report the failure with the following
behavior:
Bit Bit Description
SMBUS-6 Shall be set to 1b. See Command Code 242 for the definition of Secure Boot
7
Failure Reporting.
Shall be set to 1b. See Command Code 242 for the definition of Secure Boot
6
Failure Reporting.
199

Requirement ID Description
Shall be set to 1b and a valid Recovery code shall be entered in byte 244. These
5 codes are defined in the Platform Root-of-Trust for Recovery. Use of these codes
is explained in the OCP Hardware Secure Boot White Paper.
4:0 Reserved. Shall be cleared to zero.
The device shall take no longer than the CAP.TO timeout value to produce stable SMBus
SMBUS-7
output through the NVMe Basic Management Command (if supported).
If the device has set a non-zero value in the Error ID field (Command Code 154, byte 01h),
SMBUS-8 then the device shall clear the Drive Functional field to 0b (Command Code 0, byte 01h, Bit
5b).
The device shall generate the PEC values specified for each command code in the SMBus
SMBUS-9 data format described in Section 11.2 - NVMe Basic Management Command (Appendix A)
Data Format when the host issues a Block Read.
The device shall check the PEC value sent when the host issues a Block Write and only
process the message if the PEC value matches the SMBus data format specified value
SMBUS-10
described in Section 11.2 - NVMe Basic Management Command (Appendix A) Data Format.
The device is encouraged to issue a NACK if the PEC value is not correct.
All data returned by the NVMe Basic Management Command shall be returned in big-
SMBUS-11
endian format unless otherwise noted.

11.3 NVMe-MI Requirements
Requirement ID Description
The device shall support NVM Express Management Interface Specification, Revision 2.0 or
NVMe-MI-1 later, including all mandatory requirements. The vendor shall provide an NVMe-MI
compliance report that demonstrates compliance.
The device shall support all NVMe-MI functionality required by this specification over
NVMe-MI-2 SMBus, even when the PCIe link is not active (as required by the NVM Express Management
Interface Specification).
NVMe-MI-3 The device shall support NVMe-MI over PCIe VDM (see NVMe-MI-1).
NVMe-MI-4 The device shall support SMBus Fixed and Discoverable.
The device shall NACK any SMBus addresses not listed in the NVM Express Management
NVMe-MI-5
Interface Specification.
NVMe-MI-6 The device shall support the Get UDID command per the SMBus Specification.
NVMe-MI-7 Obsolete, see FRU-1.
204

Requirement ID Description
NVMe-MI-8 Obsolete, see NVMe-MI-2.
NVMe-MI-9 Obsolete, see NVMe-MI-3.
All mandatory NVMe Admin commands and the following optional NVMe Admin commands
shall be supported by MCTP over SMBus, and by MCTP over PCIe VDM.
• Firmware Commit
• Firmware Image Download
• Format NVM
NVMe-MI-10 • Lockdown
• Sanitize
• Security Send for TCG devices
• Security Receive for TCG devices
• Device Self-test
• Set Features
All mandatory Log Identifiers, all Log Identifiers defined in this specification, and the
following optional Log Identifiers shall be supported by MCTP over SMBus, and by MCTP
over PCIe VDM.
• Device Self-test (06h)
• Telemetry Host-Initiated (07h)
NVMe-MI-11
• Telemetry Controller-Initiated (08h)
• Persistent Event Log (0Dh)
• Command and Feature Lockdown (14h)
• Sanitize Status (81h)
• SMART / Health Information Extended (C0h)
NVMe-MI-12 Obsolete. See NVMe-MI-11.
All mandatory Feature Identifiers, all Feature Identifiers defined in this specification, and the
following Feature Identifiers shall be supported by MCTP over SMBus, and by MCTP over
PCIe VDM.
NVMe-MI-13
• Power Management (02h)
• Timestamp (0Eh)
• Temperature Threshold (04h)
The device shall support locking down all supported Admin commands and all supported
Features on the in-band interface via a Lockdown command issued out-of-band via MCTP
NVMe-MI-14
over SMBus, and by MCTP over PCIe VDM. This includes the Lockdown command itself, and
all Admin commands and Features not referenced in this specification.
The following commands are prohibited and shall return an NVMe-MI Response Message
Status of Invalid Command Opcode:
• PCIe Memory Write
NVMe-MI-15
• PCIe Memory Read
• PCIe I/O Write
• PCIe I/O Read
205

Requirement ID Description
Support for the PCIe Configuration Read command is optional.
Access to user data is prohibited via out-of-band NVMe-MI (e.g., vendor-specific commands
NVMe-MI-16
shall not access user data).
NVMe-MI-17 The device shall support SMBus/I2C Frequencies of 100 KHz and 400 KHz.
For SMBus, the device shall support all possible MCTP Transmission Unit Size values up to
NVMe-MI-18
the largest (250 bytes).
For PCIe VDM, the NVMe device shall support all possible MCTP Transmission Unit Size
NVMe-MI-19
values up to the PCIe Max Payload Size Supported.
NVMe devices shall support a minimum throughput of 50 MiB/s for data transfer in each
direction over the MCTP over PCIe VDM interface under the assumptions that:
a) there is no delay between Request Messages from the Management Controller for
transfers that require multiple Request/Response Messages; and
NVMe-MI-20 b) there is a single data transfer and no other MCTP over PCIe VDM activity at the
device.
This is a sustained throughput requirement for large transfers of 1 MiB or more (e.g.,
transfer a firmware image to the device, transfer a telemetry log page from the device) that
does not include the overhead to start and end a transfer.
Any TCG method invoked via NVMe-MI that takes longer than 100 ms shall run in the
NVMe-MI-21 background using the OutstandingData mechanism (preferred) or the More Processing
Required mechanism.
NVMe-MI-22 The device shall support NVMe-MI over SPDM Secured Messages (see SPDM-7).
The device shall support the following Asynchronous Event Messages per TP6035a and shall
support the following Asynchronous Events:
• Controller Fatal Status (Asynchronous Event ID 01h)
• Shutdown Status (Asynchronous Event ID 02h)
• Namespace Attribute Changed (Asynchronous Event ID 04h)
• Firmware Activated (Asynchronous Event ID 05h)
NVMe-MI-23 • Composite Temperature (Asynchronous Event ID 06h)
• Percentage Drive Life Used (Asynchronous Event ID 07h)
• Available Spare (Asynchronous Event ID 08h)
• SMART Warnings (Asynchronous Event ID 09h)
• Telemetry Controller-Initiated Data Available (Asynchronous Event ID 0Ah)
• PCIe Link Active (Asynchronous Event ID 0Bh)
• Sanitize Failure Mode (Asynchronous Event ID 0Ch)
If the device is in SMBus mode, and the SMBus clock is low for longer than t (refer
TIMEOUT,MIN
to the SMBus Specification), then the device shall perform SMBus clock-low recovery even if
NVMe-MI-24 firmware is hung. Refer to section 4.2.2 of the SMBus specification version 3.3.1 – the
behavior that is “highly recommended” (including the communication interface reset) is
mandatory in this specification.
206

Requirement ID Description
The device shall support retrieval of log pages greater than 4 KiB as required by the NVM
NVMe-MI-25
Express Management Interface Specification.
For devices that support auxiliary power, the device shall be fully functional including
NVMe-MI-26 NVMe-MI over SMBus/I2C as long as main power is present even if auxiliary power is
absent.
For form factors that support I3C, the device shall support I3C Basic Specification v1.1.1 as
NVMe-MI-27 specified in the NVM Express Management Interface Specification and SFF-TA-1009
Enterprise and Datacenter Standard Form Factor Pin and Signal Specification.
The device shall support the PCIe Configuration Write command for a single-byte-sized PCIe
Configuration Write to the Power Management Control/Status Register (Offset 04h) in the
PCI Power Management Capability Structure. PCIe Configuration Writes to any register
NVMe-MI-28
other than the Power Management Control/Status Register and PCIe Configuration Writes
that access any byte offset other than 4h (e.g., a multi-byte write that starts at offset 4h)
shall be aborted with a status code of Access Denied.
The device shall support multiple NVMe-MI Management Endpoints per 2-wire port (i.e.,
I2C or I3C port) via MCTP bridging for Endpoint Identifier assignment so that multiple
Management Controllers are able to manage the device via NVMe-MI. This device support
for multiple Management Endpoints shall include support for TP6034a, which is included in
NVMe-MI-29 NVMe-MI 2.0, see NVMe-MI-1.
If the device is unable to use MCTP bridging for Endpoint Identifier assignment on a 2-wire
port (e.g., because the device is unable to obtain Endpoint Identifiers for MCTP bridging to
assign to multiple NVMe-MI Management Endpoints), then the device shall use a single
NVMe-MI Management Endpoint for that 2-wire port.
If the device is in I3C mode and the I3C Clock is low for longer than the T2wrst min time (see
the SFF-TA-1009 specification), then the device shall switch to SMBus mode, even if the
NVMe-MI-30
firmware is hung. See NVMe-MI-24 for required behavior if the SMBus clock remains low
after switching to SMBus mode.
NVMe-MI-31 A device that supports I3C shall support I3C Basic SDR with a frequency of 12.5 MHz.
NVMe-MI-32 A device that supports I3C shall support I3C Basic HDR-DDR with a frequency of 12.5 MHz.
11.4 VPD Requirements
Requirement ID Description
The device shall have a VPD that is accessible over SMBus and supports IPMI Platform
FRU-1 Management FRU Information. The VPD shall support all required elements that are
defined in the NVM Express Management Interface Specification.
FRU-2 The device shall support a FRU Information Device Size of at least 512 bytes.
The device shall support the NVMe MultiRecord (i.e., Record Type ID 0Bh). The length of
FRU-3
MultiRecord shall be set to 20h to remove reserved bytes.
207

Requirement ID Description
The device shall support the NVMe PCIe MultiRecord (i.e., Record Type ID 0Ch). The length
FRU-4
of MultiRecord shall be set to 8h to remove reserved bytes.
The device shall support the following Topology MultiRecords (i.e., Record Type ID 0Dh):
• Upstream Connector Element Descriptor (i.e., Element Descriptor Type 2h);
FRU-5
• NVM Subsystem Element Descriptor (i.e., Element Descriptor Type 7h); and
• FRU Information Device Element Descriptor (i.e., Element Descriptor Type 8h).
The Maximum Power field in the Upstream Connector Element Descriptor shall indicate
FRU-6
maximum average power measured required by PCM-1.
12 Security
12.1 Basic Security Requirements
Requirement ID Description
All device firmware images shall be signed with both a classical (see SBT-1) and PQC (see
SBT-4) algorithm. The device shall validate both signatures successfully before the device
SEC-1 completes processing a Firmware Commit command that commits a firmware image and
before a firmware image is activated. Both device firmware image signatures shall be
validated on every reboot and during firmware update.
The device shall support XTS-AES-256 (as specified in NIST SP 800-38E, which references
IEEE STD 1619) or AES-256-GCM (as specified in NIST SP 800-38D) hardware-based data
encryption for performance and to prevent firmware tampering with the encryption
SEC-2
mechanism. AES-256-GCM is the preferred mode.
The combination of AES-256-CTR (as specified in NIST SP 800-38A) with HMAC-SHA256
(where the HMAC is calculated on the ciphertext) is an acceptable alternative.
The device shall support anti-rollback protection for firmware. If the Security Version
Number (see SMART-22) of the firmware being committed or activated is greater or equal to
the Security Version Number of the currently running firmware, then the firmware is
allowed to be committed or activated. If the Security Version Number of the firmware being
committed or activated is less than the Security Version Number of the currently running
SEC-3
firmware, then the firmware shall not be committed or activated.
If firmware activation occurs as a result of a power cycle, then the term “currently running
firmware” in this requirement refers to the firmware that was running immediately prior to
that power cycle.
See FWUP-8 for additional Firmware Commit command requirements.
SEC-4 The device shall support Crypto Erase (see NVMe-AD-5) and NVMe-AD-7).
SEC-5 The device shall support Secure Boot (see Section 12.2 Secure Boot).
The device shall have a method of identifying a secure boot failure which does not require
SEC-6
physical access to the device.
208

Requirement ID Description
The device’s cryptographic module shall be FIPS 140-3 level 2 capable per CMVP and shall
SEC-7
follow the NIST 800-90 (A, B and C) specification.
The device shall only implement NIST approved cryptographic algorithms and shall be
SEC-8
designed to achieve FIPS-140-3 validation (see SEC-7).
The device shall support key revocation allowing a new key to be used for firmware
SEC-9 verification. The device shall support at least 4 key revocations, and key revocation shall not
make the device unbootable (i.e., the device supports at least 5 keys).
SEC-10 Obsolete. Moved to TCG-FEATURE-1.
SEC-11 Obsolete. Moved to TCG-FEATURE-2.
SEC-12 Obsolete. Moved to TCG-FEATURE-3.
TCG devices shall support the IEEE1667 Probe (100h) and the TCG Storage Transport (104h)
SEC-13
silos. See SEC-50 and SEC-51 for additional IEEE1667 requirements.
The vendor shall follow the Security Development Lifecycle (SDL), and provide a report with
the following for each qualification-ready or production-ready firmware version:
• The Threat Model.
• Fuzz & Pen Tests.
SEC-14
• Static Analysis.
• Build Logs and Compiler Security Settings.
Additional information about the SDL is available here:
https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/sdl/default.aspx
A firmware audit of the initial firmware released to customer intended for qualification and
any subsequent firmware release intended for production use shall be performed using OCP
SAFE, Framework v1.0 or later. A Scope 1 audit is the minimum requirement. The detailed
report for each firmware release delivered to the customer shall be provided to the
SEC-15
customer.
The customer may choose to put the firmware release into production use ahead of the
vendor delivering the completed SAFE audit results (e.g., deploy hotfix firmware before the
incremental SAFE audit for that hotfix firmware is received).
All signing keys shall be stored in a Hardware Security Module (HSM) that is either FIPS
SEC-16
140-2 Level 3 (or greater) certified or FIPS 140-3 Level 3 (or greater) certified.
Access/use of signing keys should be restricted to a small set of developers, following the
SEC-17 principle of least privilege. The number of people with access and their corresponding roles
shall be provided.
All debug ports shall be disabled before the device leaves the factory. Alternatively, the
ports shall only be accessible in the field after a successful exchange of a challenge-response
SEC-18
mechanism using an asymmetric crypto scheme (see NIST SP 800-63). The state shall be
reset to inaccessible on any reset or power cycle.
All vendor unique commands, log pages or set features that are not explicitly defined in this
SEC-19
specification or approved of in writing by the customer shall be disabled before the device
209

Requirement ID Description
leaves the factory. Alternatively, the commands/log pages/set features shall only be
accessible in the field after a successful exchange of a challenge-response mechanism using
an asymmetric crypto scheme (see NIST SP 800-63). The state shall be reset to inaccessible
on any reset or power cycle.
Adversarial testing using red teams shall be conducted before the start of customer
SEC-20 qualification of the initial product and any major firmware or hardware revision. A report of
items attempted, and results shall be provided to the customer.
The vendor shall provide timely notification to the customer of security issues and delivery
of fixes to the customer:
• The vendor shall document all security fixes with each firmware update.
• The vendor shall notify end customer within 7 days of discovering security issues in
the device hardware or firmware.
• Notification of issues shall include the process and timeline of the vendor’s
SEC-21 commitment to fix the issue:
o For privately disclosed vulnerabilities, the duration shall be no longer than
90 days.
o For publicly disclosed vulnerabilities, the duration shall be no longer than 7
days.
o Vendors shall notify the customers about the known CVEs and security
issues and provide security-related updates before public announcement.
The Telemetry Controller-Initiated log page, Telemetry Host-Initiated log page, shall be
designed so that the contents of Data Area 1 and Data Area 2 are human readable after
SEC-22 decoding via the OCP plugin for the nvme-cli, see TEL-14. Telemetry Data Areas 3 and 4
should be human readable after decoding via a vendor-specific tool. The contents of Data
Area 1 and Data Area 2 shall be sufficient for debugging.
The device shall not include user data, passwords, keys, or any secret or sensitive
SEC-23
information in any Telemetry or debug log pages.
SEC-24 All public keys shall be revocable.
Secure Boot Flow shall be based upon a hardware root of trust. All mutable key(s),
SEC-25 certificate(s), and/or firmware shall be cryptographically bound to the hardware root of
trust. See Section 12.2 Secure Boot.
The device shall only update firmware via a secure firmware update flow that shall be based
SEC-26
upon immutable public keys.
SEC-27 Obsolete. Moved to TCG-CRYPTO-1.
The device shall purge all symmetric keys and all private asymmetric keys from volatile
SEC-28 memory as soon as they are no longer needed for operation during the current power on
state.
The device shall only store, even if temporarily, host provided passwords, host provided
SEC-29 keys, or any host provided secret information in non-volatile memory in an encrypted form.
The encryption key(s) for this protection shall not be stored in non-volatile memory. Device
210

Requirement ID Description
shall not store plaintext/cleartext secrets in any non-volatile memories. The device shall
protect all such stored passwords, keys, and secrets from unauthorized modification.
The vendor must deliver key management and encryption flow diagram details (not source
code) which includes:
• Encryption algorithms and modes (e.g., RNG, wrapping function, key derivation
function).
SEC-30 • Key size and password length.
• Any crypto information that is stored in nonvolatile memory.
• Critical Security Parameters.
Complete details about algorithm inputs (e.g., Initialization vector source and size, salt
source and size, unique per device/product line/vendor)
The vendor shall provide industry certification reports, once they are available such as FIPS
SEC-31
and OCP SAFE for device and device components such as TRNG, RNG, Crypto engine etc.
Log data and user data (data transferred from the Host in Write Commands) shall be stored
SEC-32 on physically separate areas on the device. For example, in the system area and the user
data area, respectively.
The vendor shall provide a comprehensive list of what is included in the logs covering both
SEC-33 the standard logs and vendor-unique logs. The list shall identify any defined optional events
or items that are not logged by the device.
SEC-34 Obsolete.
All telemetry and debug logs shall only be writable by device firmware that has been
SEC-35
verified as part of a secure boot.
SEC-36 Obsolete. Moved to TCG-AUTH-3.
SEC-37 Obsolete. Moved to NVME-MI-2 and NVME-MI-10.
SEC-38 Obsolete. Moved to TCG-FEATURE-4.
SEC-39 The device shall not allow the host to read firmware or boot code from the device.
All device firmware packages shall be encrypted based on a symmetric encryption
SEC-40
algorithm. See SEC-2 for acceptable algorithms and SEC-29 for key storage requirements.
If the device does not support Caliptra, the device shall only support activation of encrypted
SEC-41
firmware images.
If the device does not support Caliptra, the device shall only store firmware in encrypted
SEC-42 format when stored in non-volatile memory to protect against physical disassembly of drive
to extract stored firmware from media.
Sanitize, Format NVM User Data Erase/Cryptographic Erase, and TCG
SEC-43 Revert/RevertSP/GenKey functionality shall comply with the IEEE 2883-2022 Purge
requirements.
Any command that changes the media encryption key(s) as part of its operation (e.g.,
SEC-44
Sanitize command with Crypto Erase (100b), TCG Revert, TCG RevertSP, etc.), shall purge, as
211

Requirement ID Description
defined in IEEE 2883-2022, all copies of the previous key(s) before the device completes the
operation. If the device cannot guarantee that all copies of the previous media encryption
key(s) have been purged, then the device shall fail the operation.
Any optional security features supported by the device and not described in this document
SEC-45
shall be clearly documented and disclosed to the customer.
TCG devices shall support the Security Receive and Security Send commands in-band (i.e.,
SEC-46 bit 0 in the Optional Admin Command Support field in the Identify Controller data structure
shall be set to 1b).
The Cryptographic Module Boundary should be defined to minimize the size and scope of
the Cryptographic Module, and in particular the Cryptographic Module Boundary should not
encompass the entire physical device. This enables FIPS certification of the Cryptographic
Module to be leveraged across multiple device configurations and versions. To facilitate a
timelier NIST certification approval process, any revalidations made to the Cryptographic
SEC-47 Module Boundary should be Non-Security Relevant. The Cryptographic Module Boundary
shall include all relevant cryptographic functions within the boundary itself, such as the data
at rest encryption algorithms per FIPS 197 and digital signature algorithms for firmware
authentication per FIPS 186-5. The device is required to provide compliance information
that enables the host to obtain FIPS certification information that is associated with the
Cryptographic Module, see SEC-52.
At a minimum, the device shall support the following signature and hashing algorithms for
secure boot, firmware update, CoRIM, and SPDM implementations:
• ECDSA P384 or other asymmetric key signature algorithms that meet at least
192-bits of security strength as documented in NIST SP 800-57 Part 1 Revision 5
(Table 2). The device may also support RSA 3072 instead.
SEC-48 • SHA-384, SHA3-384, or other hashing algorithms that meet at least 192-bits of
security strength as documented in NIST SP 800-57 Part 1 Revision 5 (Table 3).
• ML-KEM-1024 as specified in FIPS 203.
• ML-DSA-87 as specified in FIPS 204 or one of LMS or XMSS as specified in NIST
SP800-208.
o ML-DSA-87 is preferred.
The device shall not reveal secrets (including passwords, asymmetric private keys,
symmetric keys, and any other secret information) even in encrypted form via programmatic
SEC-49
methods, logging operations (including debug outputs), and within externally accessible
configuration files or settings.
After power on, for a given ComID, any IEEE1667 functionality that is different than what is
specified by the TCG specifications (e.g., the Command Sequencing Reset differences) shall
only take effect if IEEE1667 support is enabled (see G1667-2) and the device receives a
SEC-50 Security Send or Security Receive command with the Security Protocol field set to a value of
EEh on that ComID only (i.e., IEEE1667).
Once the device receives a Security Send or Security Receive command with the Security
Protocol field set to a value of EEh on a given ComID, then the device shall behave as
212

Requirement ID Description
specified by the IEEE1667 Specification for that ComID until the next Controller Level Reset
when the device shall switch back to TCG-compliant behavior for all ComIDs.
If IEEE1667 support is enabled and the host completes taking ownership of the device (refer
to the TCG Storage Application Note: Encrypting Drives Compliant with Opal SSC) via the
Security Send/Security Receive commands with the Security Protocol field set to a value of
01h to 06h (i.e., TCG), then the device shall go into a mode where Security Send or Security
Receive command with the Security Protocol field set to a value of EEh is prohibited and
SEC-51 results in an error status code of Access Denied being returned for any Security Send or
Security Receive command with the Security Protocol field set to a EEh.
If the device is in the mode where Security Send or Security Receive command with the
Security Protocol field set to a value of EEh is prohibited, then a Revert shall cause the
device to switch back to a mode where Security Send or Security Receive command with the
Security Protocol field set to a value of EEh is allowed.
A FIPS 140 device shall support retrieval of the FIPS 140 compliance descriptor for the active
firmware via the Security Receive command with Security Protocol 00h and an SP Specific
value of 0002h, as specified in the SFSC (Security Features for SCSI Commands) SCSI
SEC-52 standard. For a FIPS 140 validated device, the contents of the FIPS 140 compliance
descriptor shall match the FIPS 140 certificate for that FIPS 140 device. This requirement
applies to all FIPS 140 devices, independent of whether or not the Cryptographic Module
Boundary encompasses the entire physical device (see SEC-47).
For a FIPS 140 device, the FIPS 140 compliance descriptor shall be populated with accurate
and complete information reflecting the device’s FIPS 140 certification information in
devices that are intended for customer qualification (i.e., Qualification Samples), production
devices, and any device that has been submitted for FIPS 140 validation (see DCLP-13).
For a FIPS 140 device, the FIPS 140 compliance descriptor shall be populated with accurate
SEC-53 and complete information reflecting the device’s FIPS 140 certification information in any
device that is intended to be FIPS 140 validated, but has not yet been submitted for FIPS 140
validation, e.g., Engineering Samples for which the expected contents of the FIPS 140
compliance descriptor are known (see DCLP-13).
These requirements override any requirements in the SCSI SFSC standard to only populate
the FIPS 140 compliance descriptor for a device that is FIPS 140 validated.
12.2 Secure Boot
The device shall support Secure Boot. There are two fundamental things to address for secure boot:
• Secure boot rooted in hardware.
• Core Root of Trust Measurement.
The vendor should follow the recommendations in the TCG Hardware Requirements for a Device Identifier
Composition Engine and the guidelines in NIST SP 800-193. DICE coupled with TCG Implicit Identity Based Device
Attestation and Source for RIoT Reference Architecture can help implement Cryptographic Identity with implicit
attestation.
213

Requirement ID Description
The device shall comply with the FIPS 186-5 Digital Signature Standard (DSS) and relevant
NIST standards for PQC Digital Signatures (see SBT-4) and the OCP Hardware Secure Boot
SBT-1 v1.0 or later specification.
This requirement does not require implementation of the OCP Attestation of System
Components specification.
SBT-2 For Core Root of Trust measurement, each device shall have a Cryptographic Device Identity.
The TCG Hardware Requirements for a Device Identifier Composition Engine v1.0 R0.91 or
SBT-3 later standard or an alternative hardware based cryptographic identity shall be
implemented.
The device shall implement at least one of the Digital Signature PQC algorithms as specified
SBT-4
in the Commercial National Security Algorithm Suite 2.0 no later than 2025.
SBT-5 Secure boot flow shall be immutable for exploitation and use immutable public keys.
The next version of this specification will require full implementation of the OCP Secure
SBT-6
Firmware Recovery specification.

The vendor should follow the guidelines in NIST SP 800-193.
Requirement ID Description
The device shall comply with the Security Protocol and Data Model (SPDM) Specification,
SPDM-1 Version 1.4 or later. The device shall be backwards compatible with the Security Protocol
and Data Model (SPDM) Specification, Version 1.1 and later.
The device shall comply with the revised PCI-SIG Component Measurement and
SPDM-2
Authentication (CMA-SPDM) ECN that was published on September 20, 2023.
SPDM-3 The device shall support SPDM-1 and SPDM-2 via MCTP over SMBus/I2C.
SPDM-4 The device shall support SPDM-1 and SPDM-2 via MCTP over PCIe VDM.
The device shall support SPDM-1 and SPDM-2 via PCI-SIG Data Object Exchange (DOE)
SPDM-5
Revision 1.1.
SPDM-6 Obsolete. See CERT-1.
The device shall comply with the Secured Messages using SPDM over MCTP Binding
SPDM-7
Specification, Version 1.1.1 or later.
The device shall comply with the Secured Messages using SPDM Specification, Version 1.1.1
SPDM-8
or later. Mutual authentication is not required.
The device shall comply with the Security Protocol and Data Model (SPDM) over MCTP
SPDM-9
Binding Specification, Version 1.0.2 or later.

SPDM-10 within WT amount of time after sending an ERROR message with an ErrorCode equal to

1)
The device shall comply with the CHALLENGE_AUTH response requirements in the following
table:
CHALLENGE_AUTH Response Requirement
SPDM-16
0h = No Measurement Summary Hash Required

Signature endianness shall follow the requirements in Security Protocol and Data Model
(SPDM) Specification, Version 1.2.2 or later even in the case that an older SPDM version is
SPDM-17 supported by the device. For example, on ECDSA signatures, the byte order for r and s shall
be big endian order. When placing ECDSA signatures into an SPDM signature field, r shall
come first, followed by s.
A device that is not ready to accept a new request message shall respond with an ERROR
response message with an ErrorCode of Busy (3h) (i.e., the device shall not silently discard
SPDM-18 the request message).
This requirement does not apply while a device is becoming ready to respond to SPDM
requests after application of main power (see SPDM-11).
If a request is received out of order, then the device shall respond with an ERROR response
message with an ErrorCode of RequestResynch (i.e., 43h) for that request and for all
SPDM-19
subsequent requests until a GET_VERSION command is received and processed (i.e., the
device shall not silently discard requests due to an out of order request).
The device shall support at least two SPDM banks in order to support both a classical (e.g.,
SPDM-20
RSA, ECDSA) certificate chain and a CNSA 2.0 compliant certificate chain (e.g., ML-DSA-87).
For form factors that support I3C, the device shall support SPDM-1 and SPDM-2 via MCTP
SPDM-21
over I3C.
12.3.1 SPDM Certificates
Requirement ID Description
The leaf certificate shall include a Subject Alternative Name certificate extension otherName
field using the DMTF OID as defined in the Security Protocol and Data Model (SPDM)
Specification with the following settings:
CERT-1 • the DMTF-serialNumber shall be set to same value reported in the Serial Number
field of the Identify Controller data structure;
• the DMTF-product shall be set to same value reported in the Model Number field of
the Identify Controller data structure; and
216

Requirement ID Description
• the DMTF-manufacturer shall be set to a value reported in the PCI Vendor ID field
using the ASCII representation of the hexadecimal value without a leading “0x” or
trailing “h”.
The Root CA Trusted Certificate Authority shall be the device vendor and shall be the same
CERT-2
across all device models developed by the device vendor.
CERT-3 Device self-signed certificates are prohibited.
The device shall support the AliasCert or DeviceCert model in slot 0. An AliasCert in slot 0 is
CERT-4 permitted while running regardless of which version of the SPDM Specification is negotiated
(e.g., AliasCert in slot 0 is permitted running in SPDM 1.1 mode).
The AliasCert chain shall contain an immutable hardware identity certificate and hardware
CERT-5 identity OID (refer to the SPDM Specification) shall be used to indicate hardware identity
certificate(s).
A Mutable certificate OID (refer to the SPDM Specification) shall be used to indicate mutable
CERT-6
certificates.
12.3.2 SPDM Firmware Measurements
Requirement ID Description
The device shall be able to generate signed measurements (i.e., MEAS_CAP field shall be set
to 10b) and shall support the following Measurement block types:
DMTFSpecMeasurementValueType Requirement
[7] - 0b: Digest, 1b: Raw Bit Stream Digest Required
[6:0] = 00h: immutable ROM Recommended
[6:0] = 01h: mutable firmware Required
SFM-1 [6:0] = 02h: hardware configuration, such as straps, debug modes Recommended
[6:0] = 03h: firmware configuration (e.g., configurable firmware policy) Recommended
[6:0] = 04h: Measurement manifest Required
[6:0] = 05h: Structured representation of debug and device mode Optional
[6:0] = 06h: Mutable firmware’s version number Optional
[6:0] = 07h: Mutable firmware’s security version number, which should
Optional
be formatted as an 8-byte unsigned integer
The device shall always return measurements of the most recently activated firmware and
SFM-2 current configuration without requiring a power cycle or any type of NVMe or PCIe reset.
Measurements of the activated firmware image are acceptable.
The device shall report the same measurements blocks and values for all devices in a
SFM-3 product family (e.g., devices with the same model but different capacity points, endurance,
or form factor).
217

| Requirement ID  |     | Description  |     |
| --------------- | --- | ------------ | --- |
The device vendor shall provide a Reference Integrity Manifest (RIM) for the firmware
modules and configuration settings for components using the CoRIM schema as defined by
SFM-4
IETF (refer to the latest version of draft-ietf-rats-corim - Concise Reference Integrity Manifest
or the RFC (if any) published from that Internet-Draft).
The reference measurements in the CoRIM schema may be expressed using the CoMID tags
and/or the CoSWID tags.  If the CoRIM has reference measurements from sub-components
SFM-5
from different manufacturers, then the reference values of the sub-components shall be
captured in CoSWID tags with their individual signatures.
The RIM shall apply to all devices in a product family (e.g., devices with the same model but
SFM-6  different capacity points, endurance, or form factor).  The RIM shall not include any instance
specific information (e.g., any device specific identifiers such as Serial Number, UUID, etc.).
The RIM shall be signed by the device manufacturer using the COSE schema (refer to RFC
9052 - CBOR Object Signing and Encryption (COSE): Structures and Process (ietf.org) and RFC
SFM-7
9053 - CBOR Object Signing and Encryption (COSE): Initial Algorithms (ietf.org)).  The device
manufacturer shall use an approved digital signature algorithm (see SEC-48).
The device manufacturer shall provide the customer with a digital certificate with the public
key that is able to be used to verify the RIM signatures.  This digital certificate shall validate
SFM-8
(e.g., via direct signature or certificate chain) to the Root CA Trusted Certificate Authority
(see CERT-2).
The RIM shall contain the hash values of each firmware module using an approved hashing
algorithm (see SEC-48).  ASCII text string values in the RIMs are acceptable if the string
SFM-9
length is less than 128 bytes and the string is descriptive (e.g., a module identifier string, a
product identifier string, or firmware revision string).

| DATAE-1  Obsolete.  Duplicate of SEC-2.  |     |              |     |
12.5 TCG Implementation Requirements

the additional requirements in this section.

12.5.1  TCG Version and Features
| Requirement ID  |     |     |     |     |     | Description  |     |
| --------------- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | ------------ | --- |
TCG devices shall support TCG Storage Security Subsystem Class: Opal Version 2.02, Revision
TCG-FEATURE-1  1.0 or later, and all mandatory feature sets (e.g., Additional DataStore, Block SID
Authentication, and PSID feature sets).
TCG devices shall support TCG Single User Mode feature set Version 1.00, Revision 2.00 or
TCG-FEATURE-2
later.
TCG devices shall support TCG Configurable Locking for NVMe Namespaces and SCSI LUNs
feature set Version 1.02, Revision 1.16 or later with mandatory support for the Namespace
TCG-FEATURE-3
Global Range Locking object.  The Namespace Non-Global Range Locking object may be
supported.
| TCG-FEATURE-4  |     | Obsolete, see TCG-FEATURE-1.  |     |     |     |     |     |
| -------------- | --- | ----------------------------- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
The current TCG feature set configuration settings, if any, shall persist through a download
and activation of firmware code (e.g., TPer Lock State, Single User Mode configuration, no
TCG-FEATURE-5
C_PIN Reset).  This is required regardless of the “default setting state” of the new code being
downloaded.
The device shall support the Data Removal Mechanism Feature Descriptor (Feature Code
TCG-FEATURE-6
0404h).  The Data Removal Time Format bit shall be set to 0 to indicate the Data Removal
219

Requirement ID Description
Time value is stored in (value x 2) seconds. The Data Removal Time shall be less than or
equal to 10 seconds per CTO-1.
The device shall support at least 8 Additional DataStore Tables, each with a minimum size of
TCG-FEATURE-7 128 KiB. The required size of these tables is in addition to the 10 MiB minimum required for
the DataStore Table.
The device shall support Shadow MBR functionality and shall disable that functionality by
TCG-FEATURE-8 default in the MBRControl Table as specified by the TCG Opal SSC standard (see TCG-
FEATURE-1).
TCG-FEATURE-9 The device should not support TCG Opal PSK Secure Messaging.
12.5.2 TCG Communication Layer
Requirement ID Description
The device shall support ComID management, and the Level 0 Discovery TPer Feature
TCG-COMM-1
Descriptor shall report ComID Mgmt supported.
TCG-COMM-2 The device shall support at least 2 Static ComIDs.
TCG-COMM-3 The device should support at least 2 Dynamic ComIDs.
TCG-COMM-4 MaxComIDTime shall be at least 120 seconds.
TCG-COMM-5 MaxComIDTime shall be greater than DefSessionTimeout.
12.5.3 TCG Session Layer
Requirement ID Description
A single Read-Write Session shall be supported per SP and shall be indicated by
MaxSessions. MaxSessions shall indicate the maximum number of simultaneous sessions
TCG-SES-1 supported (Read-Write + Read-Only). It is not required to support an active RW session on
the AdminSP at the same time as sessions on other SPs, because this would violate the TCG
Storage Architecture Core Specification.
At least 2 Read-Only Sessions shall be supported per SP and shall be indicated by
TCG-SES-2 MaxReadSessions. SET methods and other TCG commands that modify the TCG
configuration state shall be rejected during a Read Only session.
TCG-SES-3 DefSessionTimeout shall be included in the Properties Method response from the device.
TCG-SES-4 The DefSessionTimeout value shall be 90,000 ms.
TCG-SES-5 The MaxSessionTimeout value shall be 0. This value indicates that there is no limit.
TCG-SES-6 The MinSessionTimeout value should be 500 ms.
The SessionTimeout parameter of the StartSession method call shall be used to configure
TCG-SES-7
the session timeout.
TCG-SES-8 Support for setting the SPSessionTimeout column of the SPInfo table is recommended.
220

12.5.4 TCG Transactions
Requirement ID Description
TCG-TRAN-1 TCG devices shall support TCG Transactions.
TCG Nested Transactions may be supported. If TCG Nested Transactions are supported, all
TCG-TRAN-2 supported transactions including any nested transactions shall be reflected in the
MaxTransactionLimit property.
12.5.5 TCG Authentication
Requirement ID Description
TCG devices shall enforce a minimum password length (C-PIN PinLength of 16) of 16 bytes
TCG-AUTH-1
for all TCG Opal authorities.
TCG devices shall allow a password length (C-PIN PinLength of 32) of at least 32 bytes for all
TCG-AUTH-2
TCG Opal authorities.
TCG devices shall set the default TryLimit to 10 for all TCG Opal authorities. The value of the
Tries column shall only be cleared to 0 for the mandatory reasons specified in the TCG
TCG-AUTH-3
Storage Architecture Core Specification (e.g., do not clear the Tries column via the Set
method, do clear it upon successful authentication or power cycle).
Authentication of each C_PIN shall be delayed in order to limit how fast the next
authentication of that C_PIN can occur.
• The delay shall be at least 100 ms and should not exceed 250 ms and I/O shall not be
blocked during this time.
TCG-AUTH-4 • The delay shall apply regardless of whether the authentication is successful.
• The device manufacturer shall supply documentation with the implemented delay
value.
• The time limit should be enforced cryptographically (e.g., by tuning the number of
PBKDF iterations to reach the target time).
TCG-AUTH-5 The Persistence column shall be set to false for all C_PIN rows.
12.5.6 TCG Crypto
Requirement ID Description
If TCG Opal Locking SP has been activated and the host has supplied at least one authority
password, the device shall use at least one authority password as an added source of
randomness for its Deterministic Random Number Generator (DRNG).
For example, the device may use KDF (PBKDF2) on the user provided locking range
TCG-CRYPTO-1 password to generate an output of equal length to the required locking range key length
plus DRNG seed length. This output can then be utilized in parts, one part as Opal locking
range key and the other part as an additional input to the DRNG. If the DRNG
implementation does not allow the use of additional input, then an alternative option
would be to XOR this output (e.g., from PBKDF2 operation) with initial DRNG seed.
221

12.5.7 TCG Locking Security Provider
Requirement ID Description
The number of Additional Locking Ranges supported shall be at least 8 and shall be greater
TCG-LOCKING-1
than or equal to the maximum number of NVMe namespaces supported on the device.
TCG-LOCKING-2 The Locking SP of the device shall support at least one User per Locking Range.
TCG-LOCKING-3 The K_AES_256 Table shall be supported.
The K_AES_256 Table’s Key columns shall not be readable by the host or be accessible
TCG-LOCKING-4
outside the device in any manner.
Any attempt to remove the Power Cycle reset type from a LockOnReset column set value
TCG-LOCKING-5
shall be rejected.
TCG-LOCKING-6 The Locking SP of the device shall support at least 4 Admins.
12.5.8 TCG PSID Feature Set
Requirement ID Description
The PSID shall not be deterministic, shall comprise at least 160 bits of entropy. The entropy
shall be unique for each device.
The PSID shall not be derived from any information that is available without physical access
to the device.
For example, the PSID shall not be the same as the MSID, the PSID shall not be derived from
TCG-PSID-1
the device serial number or the date of manufacture because these can be read via the
device interface or obtained from other documentation. The PSID shall not be the serial
number of the drive hashed with a secret string shared with any other device or among all
devices, because the entropy shall be unique for each device.
The presence of the PSID on the device label does not violate this requirement.
The PSID shall consist of 32 ASCII characters. The allowed ASCII characters are upper case
letters, lower case letters and the digits 0-9. The characters ‘I’, ‘l’, ‘O’ and ’o’ (i.e., 49h, 6Ch,
TCG-PSID-2
4Fh and 6Fh) and the digits ‘0’ and ‘1’ (i.e., 30h and 31h) shall not be used to limit possible
visual confusion.
TCG-PSID-3 The generation method for the PSID shall be documented and provided to the customer.
After the PSID is provisioned in manufacturing, the PSID shall not be persistently stored in a
form that makes retrieval or reconstruction of the PSID by firmware possible, either on the
drive or outside the drive (e.g., it is acceptable to store the PSID on the drive hashed via a
TCG-PSID-4
cryptographic hash or KDF such that the hashed PSID can only be used to verify a PSID input
from the host).
The presence of the PSID on the device label does not violate this requirement.
Once manufacturing is complete, the PSID shall not be stored anywhere other than on the
TCG-PSID-5
physical drive label.
222

13 Device Profiles
The following are device profiles.  This section is intended to be firmware-based configuration settings
configured by device vendors when manufacturing a device.  A device may be configured with a mix of A and/or
B settings.  Each customer shall provide their A/B preference for each configuration setting.
The following conventions are used for the Device Profile Table:

| P   | Prohibited.  This shall not be supported.  |     |     |

•  M.2: the label shall be placed on the top side of the device as defined in the PCI-SIG
M.2 form factor specification.

as defined in the SFF-TA-1007 form factor specification.

E3: the primary label shall contain the drive information (e.g., model number, serial
number, manufacturing info, firmware revision) and be placed on the top label area
as defined in the SFF-TA-1008 form factor specification.  If more space is needed a
label may also be placed on the bottom label area with regulatory marks.

15 Compliance
15.1 ROHS Compliance
Requirement ID Description
The vendor shall provide component-level reporting on the use of listed materials by
ROHS-1
concentration (ppm) for all homogenous materials.
15.2 ESD Compliance
Requirement ID Description
Device manufacturer shall provide ESD immunity level (HBM - Human Body Model)
ESD-1
measured in accordance with IEC-61000-4-2.
15.3 EMC Compliance
Requirement ID Description
The device shall comply with the requirements of FCC / EN55032 Class B Radiated
EMC-1
Emissions.
16 Shock and Vibration
The shock and vibration specifications for storage devices are in the following table:
Requirement ID Description
The non-operational shock requirement is 700G, half-sine, 0.5 ms, total 6 shocks, along all
SV-1
three axes (+/-).
The vibration requirement during operation is: 1.8G , 5-500-5 Hz, Random Vibe, 20 min
SV-2 rms
along all three axes.
The vibration requirement during non-operation is: 3.13G , 5-800-5 Hz, total 6 sweeps
SV-3 rms
along all three axes, 20 minutes per sweep.
Validation flow for Shock and Vibration:
1. UUT (Unit Under Test), test fixture should be visually inspected and ensured that
everything is torqued or secured as needed. Pictures of test fixture with and w/o UUT
should be provided.
SV-4 2. Baseline performance of device should be gathered and used as a reference against post
S&V data to ensure no performance impact incurred.
3. Once S&V testing is completed, repeat visual inspection to the UUT and test fixture to
ensure no physical damage or performance impact has occurred to the UUT or test
fixture.
230

Requirement ID Description
4. Re-run stress test on the UUT in case of non-op test and provide data indicating no
performance impact incurred to the unit.
17 Sustainability Requirements
The following are the sustainability requirements for devices.
Requirement ID Description
A Life Cycle Assessment (LCA) aligned with ISO 14040 for the device shall be provided to the
SUS-1
customer.
SUS-2 Recycled content information per material type shall be provided to the customer.
18 Linux NVMe-CLI Plug-In Requirements
18.1 NVMe-CLI Management Utility

the management utilities for NVMe devices.

The vendor must test their SSDs with this utility and ensure compatibility with their device
UTIL-1 and functionality supported by OCP plugin for the nvme-cli (version 2.10 or later) (e.g.,
Format, Secure Erase, Firmware Update, etc.).

Performance Test Drive Configuration
20.3 Trim Rate Targets
• This test measures raw trim performance with no background I/O.
• 64M trim >= 50 GiB/s & <= 10 ms P99 trim latency.
• 3GB trim >= 500 GiB/s & <= 10 ms P99 trim latency.
20.4 IO.go Benchmark Targets
• This test measures how long the file system is blocked from writing/overwriting a file while a different
file is deleted.
• Less than 4 file sizes total with latency outliers > 10 ms.
• No more than 2 latency outliers per file size.
• No single latency outlier above 15 ms.
• The IO.go targets will be met with XFS, EXT-4 & BTRFS file systems.
20.5 Fileappend Benchmark Targets
• This test measures how long the file system is blocked from appending to a file while a different file is
deleted.
• No measurable stalls reported by this tool.
• Max acceptable latency outlier is 10 ms when deleting 1 GiB or 2 GiB file.
• Test should be executed for xfs, ext4 and btrfs file systems.
241

20.6 Sequential Write Bandwidth
• Full device (all available user capacity, all namespaces) must be written/filled in 180 minutes or less.
• Simple single-threaded sequential write FIO script to fill device.
20.7 CacheBench Targets
• A benchmarking tool that is a supplement for FB FIO Synth Flash tool on measuring performance for
cache applications. This is different than the “B Cache” workload in FB FIO Synth Flash.
• Two workloads need to be tested:
o Graph Cache Leader
o Kvcache WC
• The final allocator and throughput stats from the benchmark will be used to see if the targets are met.
• Send SSD latency versus time file to Facebook using one of the following methods:
o Send the raw results log file.
o Run the “extract_latency.sh script and return the raw results log file, “.tsv” and “.png” files.
• Vendor nvme-cli plugin with “physical NAND bytes written” metric in the SMART / Health Information
Extended log page (Log Identifier C0h) needs to be working to get the write amplification.
Read Latency (us)

This test measures load on a Boot Device in a stacked environment.
• Download the tool from: github.com/liu-song-6/bootbench.

22 Latency Monitoring Feature Set Theory of Operation
22.1 Overview
Latency outliers are very undesirable in the data center. The goal of this feature is to allow production
monitoring of SSD QOS outliers and to debug outlier issues in production. This feature will allow vendors and
hyperscale companies to clearly understand if the outliers are caused by the SSD or other components in the
Host system. This feature enables vendors to effectively debug latency issues efficiently. This feature will enable
predicting when latency outliers are growing and likely to impact hyperscale customers. This feature enables
many use cases involving understanding and debugging latency issues at scale in a production environment.
22.2 Functional Operation
Latency Monitoring Feature Description
Following is the high-level theory of operation describing how the Latency Monitoring feature works. The
latency of an individual command shall be measured from the time a controller fetches the command from the
SQ to the time when controller writes the CQ entry for the SQ entry it fetched.
243

22.2.1 Bucket Description Overview
There are two types of buckets Active Buckets and Static Buckets. Active Buckets are buckets that are updated in
real time. Static Buckets are buckets which are loaded with snapshots from the Active Buckets. This is a move
from the Active Buckets to the Static Buckets, thus the old values in the Static Buckets are discarded. The Static
Buckets allow hyperscale users to sample the Static Buckets over a fixed time period to gather statistics.
22.2.2 Active Bucket Description
The high-level concept is to create 4 real time buckets groups of active latency tracking command counters. Each
bucket will count latency events which exceed a configured latency threshold. A description of each bucket is in
the following figure:
Each bucket contains the following:
• Saturating Read Command Counter with an associated Measured Latency and Latency Timestamp.
• Saturating Write Command Counter with an associated Measured Latency and Latency Timestamp.
• Saturating Deallocate/TRIM Command Counter with an associated Measured Latency and Latency
Timestamp.
For clarity, the opcode to Counter mapping is in the following table:
Bucket Counter Opcode Command
Read Command Counter 02h Read
Write Command Counter 01h Write
244

Bucket Counter Opcode Command
09h with
Deallocate/TRIM Command Counter Dataset Management
Attribute – Deallocate (AD) = 1
In addition to the command counters there is a Measured Latency data structure, and a Latency Timestamp data
structure associated with each command counter. The Measured Latency and Latency Timestamp have a direct
relationship such that both are updated, or neither are updated. The Measured Latency and Latency Timestamp
will be described later in this document.
22.2.3.1 Active Command Counter Behavior
The active command counters count Read commands, Write commands, and Deallocate/TRIM commands which
exceed a configured latency threshold. These active command counters count until the command counter
saturates or the Active Bucket Timer expires. The behavior for each of these events is as follows:
• Active Command Counter Saturation:
o If the Command Counter saturates, the counter shall maintain the active value and not wrap.
• Active Bucket Timer Expiration:
o If the Active Bucket Timer Expires, then the following occurs:
• The Active Bucket Command Counter values and associated information are moved into Static Bucket
Command Counters; the Active Bucket Command Counters are then cleared to zero and re-start
counting.
• The active command counters shall count regardless of how the Active Latency Minimum Window is
configured.
22.2.3.2 Active Bucket Thresholds
There are multiple Active Command Counter Buckets. The configured latency thresholds determine which
Bucket the command counter shall be incremented in. The following figure shows how there are multiple
Buckets and thresholds for each Bucket:
245

If the Read, Write, Deallocate/TRIM command completion time is below Threshold A then no counter is
incremented. If the threshold is equal or greater than A and less than B, then the corresponding command
counter in Active Bucket 0 increments. If it is equal to or greater than B and less than threshold C, then the
corresponding command counter in Active Bucket 1 increments. If it is equal to or greater than C and less than
threshold D, then the corresponding command counter in Active Bucket 2 increments. If it is equal to or greater
than threshold D, then the corresponding command counter in Active Bucket 3 increments. By following this
process all latencies greater than threshold A are counted for Read, Write and Deallocate/TRIM commands.
When configuring the Latency Monitor Feature the thresholds shall always be configured such that Active
Threshold A < Active Threshold B < Active Threshold C < Active Threshold D.
22.2.3.3 Active Bucket Timer Behavior
The Active Bucket Timer times how long the Bucket Command Counters have been counting. When the Active
Bucket Timer is equal to the Active Bucket Timer Threshold then the following operations shall occur:
• The following data is moved:
o Active Bucket Counters 0 - 3 are moved to Static Bucket Counters 0 - 3.
o Active Latency Timestamps are moved to Static Latency Timestamps.
o Active Measured Latencies are moved to Static Measured Latencies.
o Active Latency Timestamp Units are moved to Static Latency Timestamp Units.
• The Active Bucket items shall then be updated as follows:
o Active Bucket Counters 0 - 3 are cleared to zero.
o Active Latency Timestamps are set to invalid (FFFF_FFFF_FFFF_FFFFh).
o Active Measured Latencies are cleared to zero.
o Active Latency Timestamp Units are cleared to zero.
o The Active Latency Minimum Window, if it is running, may be reset or continue to count.
o Active Bucket Timer is cleared to zero and starts the process of counting over.
246

o When looking at the data structures in the Latency Monitor log page (Log Identifier C3h) it
should be noted that the data in item #1 and #2 above is 16-byte aligned, and the data can be
moved simply by doing a data move of the entire data structure.
22.2.3.4 Active Latency Timestamp Format
The format of the Latency Timestamp follows the Timestamp data structure which is defined in the NVM Express
Base Specification. The Latency Timestamp allows an understanding of where a latency excursion occurred in
terms of wall clock time. The Latency Timestamp time reported shall be based on CQ completion.
If the device receives a Timestamp Set Features (Feature Identifier 0Eh), then the device shall use this baseline
wall clock time plus the time in milliseconds since the Timestamp was set to determine the Latency Timestamp
of the latency event. If the device receives multiple Timestamp Set Features (Feature Identifier 0Eh) the most
recent Timestamp shall be used as the baseline.
If the device does not receive Set Features with a Timestamp, then the Latency Timestamp shall be generated
based on Power on Hours.
If the device receives a Set Features with a Timestamp and then the device is powered off. When the device is
powered on it shall use the most recent Timestamp it received even if this Timestamp was from before the
device was powered off.
The Active Latency Timestamp Units shall be populated when the Latency Timestamp is updated to indicate if
the Latency Timestamp used Timestamp with Power on Hours to generate the Latency Timestamp or if only
Power on Hours were used to generate the Latency Timestamp.
22.2.3.5 Active Measured Latency and Active Latency Timestamp Updates
The Active Measured Latency is the latency measured from fetching the command in the SQ to updating the CQ.
The Active Measured Latency data structure and the Active Latency Timestamp data structure shall be updated
atomically. They shall not update independently. Each Command Counter (Read/Write/Deallocate) has an
Active Measured Latency, and an Active Latency Timestamp structure associated with it. The Active Latency
Configuration is used to configure this feature.
When the Latency Mode in the Active Latency Configuration is cleared to zero then the following behavior shall
be followed:
• The Active Measured Latency and Active Latency Timestamp will be loaded the first time the command
counter associated with it increments.
• The Active Measured Latency and Active Latency Timestamp will not be loaded again until the Active
Measured Latency is reset.
If the Latency Mode is set to 0001h in the Active Latency Configuration, then every time the associated
command counter is incremented the Active Measured Latency will report the largest measured latency based
on the associated command counter. The Active Latency Timestamp will report the time when the largest
latency occurred.
The Active Latency Minimum window also affects when the Active Measured Latency and the Active Latency
Timestamp are updated. This is described in the section on Active Latency Minimum Window.
22.2.3.6 Active Latency Minimum Window
This affects both the Active Measured Latency and the Active Latency Timestamp. This defines the minimum
time between updating the Active Measured Latency and the Active Latency Timestamp for a single Active
Bucket/Counter combination. The feature is only used if the Active Latency Mode is set to 0001h.
247

If the Active Latency Minimum Window timer is running and the Measured Latency and Latency Timestamp have
been updated, then the Latency Timestamp and Active Measured Latency will not be updated again until the
Active Latency Minimum Window timer has expired. Some examples of this are as follows:
Example 1:
Assume:
• Active Latency Minimum Window of 5 seconds.
• Latency Mode is Configured for Largest Latency.
• Bucket 2 has a threshold range of 40 ms to 400 ms.

are recorded.
The Active Latency Minimum Window acts as a filter to ensure there are not a large number of events to update
the Active Measured Latency and the Latency Timestamp. Thus, if the queue depth is 128 commands deep and
there is a latency event, then there are not 128 updates to these data structures. Rather the first event is
recorded, and the rest of the events are filtered out. It should be noted that the Active Latency Window is not
enforced across power cycles. Thus, after a power cycle the Active Latency Window shall not start until a Bucket
Counter is incremented.
22.2.3.7 Static Bucket Description
In addition to the real-time buckets there are static buckets. When the Active Bucket Timer reaches its
configured threshold (Active Bucket Timer Threshold) the active real time buckets shall be loaded into the static
buckets and the active real time buckets shall be reset and start counting from 0. The following figure describes
this:
249

22.3 Persistence Across Power Cycles
When either a safe or unsafe power transition happens the counters and associated Latency Monitoring
Information shall be saved such that they can be restored on the next power up transition and continue from
where the power cycle left off. There are additional details about this in the C.5 Latency Monitoring Feature -
Challenging Event Handling section.
22.4 Debug Logs
The Latency Monitoring Feature can also enable debug logs to trigger. The Debug Log Trigger Enable configures
which counters shall trigger a debug log the first time the Bucket/Counter combination is incremented. Only a
single debug log shall be generated. Once a Latency Monitor debug log is generated, until the Latency Monitor
debug log is discarded another Latency Monitor debug log cannot be generated.
If the Host Initiated Telemetry format supported bit is cleared to 0b then the host is able to discard the Latency
Monitor debug log by using Set Features for the Latency Monitor or by reading the Latency Monitor Debug Log.
If the Host Initiated Telemetry format supported bit is set to 1b then the host is only able to discard the Latency
Monitor debug log by using Set Features for the Latency Monitor. Reading the Latency Monitor Debug Log does
not clear the log.
The Set Features for the Latency Monitor has two mechanisms for discarding the Debug Log. One method
discards the debug log and resets the Latency Monitor feature to a new set of configured values based on the
fields in Set Features. The other method discards the Debug Log and has no effect on any of the other features
associated with the Latency Monitor Feature. Thus, the Latency Monitor Feature will keep running undisturbed
when the Debug Log is discarded.
When the Latency Monitor debug log trigger event happens, the following data shall be captured: Debug Log
Measured Latency, Debug Log Latency Timestamp, Debug Log Trigger Source, Debug Log Timestamp Units,
Debug Log Pointer as well as internal information required to debug the issue to root cause.
250

When the Host Initiated Telemetry format supported bit is set to 1b then the format of the Latency Monitor shall
follow the Host and Controller Initiated Log format.
22.5 Latency Monitoring Feature - Event Handling
22.5.1 Power Off/On When Latency Monitoring Feature is Enabled
When powering off, the Active Bucket Information (Counters, Measured Latency, Latency Timestamp, Active
Bucket Timer) may be slightly off due to concerns with flushing data with unsafe power down. The Active Bucket
Information shall maintain coherency compared to itself when flushing data with unsafe power down. When the
device powers back on the Latency Monitoring Feature shall restore the Active/Static Bucket/Debug Information
including loading the Active Bucket Counter. Once the restoration is complete then the device shall resume the
Latency Monitor functionality. The device shall start capturing latency data within 2 minutes of power on. Thus,
commands for the first 2 minutes may not be monitored. The Active Latency Window is not enforced across
power cycles. Thus, after a power cycle the Active Latency Window shall not start until a Bucket Counter is
incremented.
251

22.5.2 Latency Monitoring Feature Persistence
The Latency Monitoring Feature disabled/enabled state shall be persistent across all resets and power cycles.
When the Latency Monitor Feature is enabled the associated Latency Monitor configuration information in the
Latency Monitor log page shall persist across all resets and power cycles.
22.5.3 Moving Information from Active to Static Buckets
When moving data from the active buckets to static buckets it can be challenging to track all the information.
The Active counter shall restart counting no longer than 3 seconds from moving data from Active to Static
Counters.
22.5.4 Firmware Update
When activating new firmware, if the Latency Monitoring Feature is enabled, the firmware activation shall reset
the Latency Monitoring Feature just as if a Set Features command to enable the feature was received. The
Latency Monitoring Log shall start updating properly within 2 minutes of firmware activation completing. Thus,
there are command latencies which could be missed after initially activating new firmware.
22.6 Configuring Latency Monitoring
The Set Features command is used to configure this feature. When the Set Features command is used to
configure this feature all the data structures in both the Active and Static Buckets are reset. The debug log and
related debug information is reset based on the Discard Debug Log Field.
